1469317_11_ITEM1_P0_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. (the Partnership ) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009 and commenced operations following an initial closing on October 1, 2009.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P0_S1	The Partnership is a commodity pool engaged in speculative trading across a broad range of futures contracts and currencies.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P0_S2	The Partnership may in the future trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts (together with futures contracts and currencies, Commodity Interests ).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P1_S0	Under the Partnership s Agreement of Limited Partnership (the Limited Partnership Agreement ), Altegris Portfolio Management, Inc. (d/b/a Altegris Funds), an Arkansas corporation ( Altegris Funds or the General Partner ), serves as general partner of the Partnership and has sole responsibility for management and administration of all aspects of the Partnership s business.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P1_S1	Investors purchasing limited partnership interests (the Interests ) in the Partnership ( Limited Partners and together with the General Partner, Partners ) have no rights to participate in the management of the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P2_S0	Altegris Funds is registered with the Commodity Futures Trading Commission ( CFTC ) as a Commodity Pool Operator ( CPO ), and is a member of National Futures Association ( NFA ).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P2_S1	Quantitative Investment Management LLC, a Virginia limited liability company formed in May 2003, acts as the Partnership s trading advisor ( QIM or the Advisor ).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P2_S2	QIM became registered as a Commodity Trading Advisor ( CTA ) in 2004 and a CPO in 2005 and is a member of NFA.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P2_S3	Effective as of December 31, 2010, Altegris Funds became a wholly-owned subsidiary of Genworth Financial, Inc. ( Genworth ).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P2_S4	Genworth became a principal of Altegris Funds and Altegris Futures, L.L.C. ( Altegris Futures ), an affiliate of the General Partner, in January 2011.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P3_S0	Altegris Investments, Inc. ( Altegris ), an affiliate of the General Partner, serves as a selling agent of the Interests and acted as the Partnership s introducing broker until January 1, 2011, when Altegris Futures replaced Altegris as the Partnership s introducing broker ( Introducing Broker ).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P3_S1	Altegris Futures is registered with the CFTC as an Introducing Broker.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P4_S0	The Partnership s term will end upon the first to occur of the following: receipt by the General Partner of an election to dissolve the Partnership at a specified time by Limited Partners owning more than 50% of the Interests then outstanding, notice of which is sent by registered mail to the General Partner not less than ninety (90) days prior to the effective date of such dissolution; withdrawal, admitted or court decreed insolvency or dissolution of the General Partner unless at such time there is at least one remaining General Partner in the Partnership; or any event that makes it unlawful for the existence of the Partnership to be continued or requiring termination of the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P5_S0	The Partnership is not required to be, and is not, registered under the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P6_S0	As of February 28, 2011, the aggregate net asset value of the Interests in the Partnership before redemptions was $127,683,106.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P6_S1	The Partnership operates on a calendar fiscal year and has no subsidiaries.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P7_S0	The Partnership offers three classes of Interests: Class A, Class B and Institutional Interests (each, a Class of Interest ).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P7_S1	The Classes of Interests differ from each other only in the fees that they pay and the applicable investment minimums.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P8_S0	The Partnership s business constitutes only one segment for financial reporting purposes i.e. , a speculative commodity pool.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P8_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P8_S2	Financial information regarding the Partnership s business is set forth in the Partnership s financial statements, included herewith.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P9_S0	The Partnership s objective is to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P10_S0	QIM believes that financial markets are not entirely efficient and that numerous small inefficiencies exist and can be exploited through the prudent use of robust analysis and predictive technologies.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P11_S0	QIM currently employs several thousand quantitative trading models that utilize pattern recognition to predict short-term price movements in global futures markets.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P11_S1	All models are tested across large data sets that expose them to a wide range of market, economic, and political environments, as well as a wide range of time frames and interactions.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P11_S2	Only those models that prove to be the most robust, statistically significant, and conceptually diverse are used in actual trading.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P11_S3	The resultant system of models offers what QIM believes to be reliable signals that guide market timing and trade allocation.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P12_S0	QIM s trading strategies and models may be revised from time to time as a result of ongoing research and development seeking to devise new strategies and systems as well as to improve current methods.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P12_S1	The strategies and systems used by QIM in the future may differ significantly from those currently in use due to changes resulting from this research, and Limited Partners will not be informed of these changes as they may occur.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P13_S0	QIM applies risk management procedures that take into account the price, size, volatility, liquidity, and inter-relationships of the contracts traded.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P13_S1	The Partnership s positions are generally balanced in a manner that allocates approximately equal amounts of measured risk to as many distinct markets as possible and during significant drawdowns in equity, QIM will reduce market exposure by scaling back the Partnership s overall leverage.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P14_S0	QIM s trading is generally approximately 95% systematic and 5% discretionary.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P14_S1	All facets of the predictive models, risk management, and trade allocation are fully automated or proceduralized.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P14_S2	In this sense, the trading is systematic.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P14_S3	Discretion of QIM, however, plays a significant role in the pursuit of improvements to the Program.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P15_S0	QIM has different time horizons for the execution of certain trades.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P15_S1	For example, QIM may have certain trades executed at the beginning of the trading day while giving the executing broker limited discretion with respect to other trades.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P16_S0	QIM currently trades or monitors over 50 tradable markets in currencies, stock indices, interest rates, energy, grains, softs and metals.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P16_S1	QIM may add or delete markets from this universe of tradable markets in its discretion if QIM s research demonstrates that such an addition or deletion would enhance the program s performance.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P17_S0	All markets are futures markets or interbank currency markets.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P18_S0	QIM seeks to profitably trade each of these markets while taking advantage of the diversification available from such a varied universe of futures contracts.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P18_S1	QIM s trading program often takes opposing long and short positions within the same or related classes of correlated futures, which, taken in conjunction with the effect of diversification across a broad range of contracts, generally results in reduced market exposure than trading a single market with similar leverage.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P19_S0	A substantial portion of the equity in the Partnership s account is invested in U.S. government and agency securities and other liquid, high-quality instruments at the direction of the Custodian (as defined below).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P20_S0	QIM will target an average margin to equity level of between 5% and 20%.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P20_S1	The actual percentage of assets committed to margin at any time may be higher or lower than the target level.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P21_S0	and available for trading by QIM in Commodity Interests on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P21_S1	Interest on Partnership assets held at Newedge USA in cash or Treasury securities will be credited to the Partnership as described under Charges.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P21_S2	Depending on market factors, the amount of margin or option premiums held at Newedge USA could change significantly, and all of the Partnership s assets are available for use as margin.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P21_S3	The Partnership may also retain other brokers and/or dealers from time to time to clear or execute a portion of Partnership trades made by QIM.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P22_S0	With respect to Partnership assets not held at Newedge USA as described above, but deposited with Wilmington Trust Company (the Custodian ), the portion not held in checking, money market or other bank accounts (and used to pay Partnership operating expenses) will be invested in liquid, high-quality short-term securities at the direction of the Custodian or its sub-advisor, Wilmington Trust Investment Management, LLC, an affiliate of the Custodian that is registered with the Securities and Exchange Commission ( SEC ) as an investment adviser.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P22_S1	The Partnership s custody and investment management agreement with the Custodian permits the Custodian to invest in U.S. government and agency securities, other securities or instruments guaranteed by the U.S. government or its agencies, CDs, time deposits, banker s acceptances, commercial paper and repurchase agreements subject in each case to specific diversification, credit quality and maturity limitations.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P22_S2	The Custodian may use sub-advisers to attempt to increase yield enhancement.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P22_S3	The General Partner may direct that a portion of Partnership assets be deposited with other custodians and retain other sub-advisers for the purpose of attempting to increase yield enhancement via other cash management arrangements.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P23_S0	The percentage of the Partnership s assets deposited with these firms is also subject to change in the General Partner s sole discretion.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P23_S1	The Partnership s assets will not be commingled with the assets of any other person.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P23_S2	Depositing the Partnership s assets with banks or Newedge USA, or other clearing brokers, as segregated funds is not commingling for these purposes.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P24_S0	The Partnership pays all of its ongoing liabilities, expenses and costs.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P25_S0	Altegris Funds receives a management fee of 0.104% of the month-end net asset value, before deduction for any accrued incentive fees related to the current quarter (the management fee net asset value ), of all Class A Interests (1.25% per annum), 0.104% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Class B Interests (1.25% per annum) and 0.0625% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Institutional Interests (0.75% per annum).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P25_S1	QIM receives a 30% of quarterly trading profits applicable to each Class of Interest.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P26_S0	Each selling agent selling Class A Interests receives 0.166% of the month-end net asset value of the Partnership apportioned to each Class A Interest sold by such selling agent (2% per annum) and may elect to receive 0.0417% of the month-end net asset value apportioned to any Institutional Interest sold by such selling (0.50% per annum).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P27_S0	Newedge USA paid Altegris during 2010 and will pay Altegris Futures from and after January 1, 2011 a portion of the brokerage commissions and transaction fees received from the Partnership as well as a portion of the interest income received on the Partnership s assets.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P28_S0	Monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P28_S1	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P28_S2	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership pays only the amount described in (A) above.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P29_S0	The Partnership generally pays its operating expenses as they are incurred.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P29_S1	However, during the first twelve months after the Partnership commenced trading, the General Partner agreed to limit the operating expenses paid by the Partnership to 1/12 th of 0.5% of the month-end capital account balances of all Interests for such month.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P30_S0	A fixed administrative fee is charged to Class A and Class B Interests and paid to Altegris Funds equal to 0.0275% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balance of all such Class A and Class B Interests (0.333% per annum).
1469317_11_ITEM1_P31_S0	The CFTC has delegated to NFA responsibility for the registration of commodity trading advisors, commodity pool operators, futures commission merchants, introducing brokers and their respective associated persons and floor brokers and floor traders.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S0	The Commodity Exchange Act requires commodity pool operators such as Altegris Funds, commodity trading advisors such as QIM and commodity brokers or FCMs such as Newedge USA and introducing brokers such as Altegris Futures to be registered and to comply with various reporting and record keeping requirements.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S1	CFTC regulations also require FCMs and certain introducing brokers to maintain a minimum level of net capital.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S2	In addition, the CFTC and certain commodities exchanges have established limits referred to as speculative position limits on the maximum net long or net short speculative positions that any person may hold or control in any particular futures or options contracts traded on U.S. commodities exchanges.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S3	All accounts owned or managed by QIM will be combined for position limit purposes.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S4	QIM could be required to liquidate positions held for the Partnership in order to comply with such limits.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S5	Any such liquidation could result in substantial costs to the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P32_S6	In addition, many futures exchanges impose limits beyond which the price of a futures contract may not trade during the course of a trading day, and there is a potential for a futures contract to hit its daily price limit for several days in a row, making it impossible for QIM to liquidate a position and thereby experiencing a dramatic loss.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P33_S0	Currency forward contracts currently are not subject to regulation by any U.S. government agency.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P34_S0	In addition to such registration requirements, the CFTC and certain commodity exchanges have established limits on the maximum net long or net short position which any person may hold or control in particular commodities.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P34_S1	Most exchanges also limit the changes in futures contract prices that may occur during a single trading day.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P35_S0	In January 2011, the CFTC proposed a separate position limits regime for 28 so-called exempt (i.e. metals and energy) and agricultural futures and options contracts and their economically equivalent swap contracts.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P35_S1	Position limits in spot months are proposed to be 25% of the official estimated deliverable supply of the underlying commodity and in a non-spot month a percentage of the average aggregate 12-month rolling open interest in all months (swaps and futures) for each contract.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P35_S2	The General Partner believes that the proposed limits are sufficiently large that if adopted, they should not restrict the Partnership s trading strategy.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P36_S0	Currency forward contracts are not currently subject to regulation by any United States ( U.S. ) Government agency.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P37_S0	The Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act (the Reform Act ) was enacted in July 2010.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P37_S1	The Reform Act includes provisions that comprehensively regulate the over-the-counter derivatives markets for the first time.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P37_S2	The Reform Act will mandate that a substantial portion of over-the-counter derivatives must be executed in regulated markets and submitted for clearing to regulated clearinghouses.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P37_S3	The mandates imposed by the Reform Act may result in the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees with respect to any swaps entered into by the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P38_S0	The Reform Act also amended the definition of eligible contract participant, and the CFTC is interpreting that definition in a such manner that the Partnership may no longer be permitted to engage in forward currency transactions by directly accessing the interbank market.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P38_S1	Rather, when the Reform Act goes into effect in July 2011, the Partnership may be limited to engaging in retail forex transactions which could limit the Partnership s potential forward currency counterparties to futures commission merchants and retail foreign exchange dealers.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P38_S2	Limiting on the Partnership s potential forward currency counterparties in this manner could lead to the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P38_S3	The retail forex markets could also be significantly less liquid than the interbank market.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P38_S4	Moreover, the creditworthiness of the futures commission merchants and retail foreign exchange dealers with which the Partnership may be required to trade could be significantly weaker than the creditworthiness of the financial institutions with which the Partnership currently engages for its forward currency transactions.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P38_S5	Although the impact of requiring the Partnership to conduct forward currency transactions in the retail market could be substantial, the full scope is currently unknown and the ultimate effect could also be negligible.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P39_S0	The Partnership has no operations in foreign countries although it trades on foreign exchanges and other non-U.S. markets.
1469317_11_ITEM1_P39_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.
1469317_11_ITEM2_P0_S0	The Partnership does not own or use any physical properties in the conduct of its business.
1469317_11_ITEM2_P0_S1	Employees of Altegris, a wholly owned subsidiary of Genworth Financial, Inc. as of December 31, 2010, perform all administrative services for the Partnership from offices at 1202 Bergen Parkway, Suite 212, Evergreen, Colorado 80439 or at 1200 Prospect St., Suite 400, La Jolla, California 92037.
1469317_11_ITEM3_P0_S0	The Partnership is not aware of any pending legal proceedings to which either the Partnership is a party or to which any of its assets are subject.
1469317_11_ITEM3_P0_S1	The Partnership is not aware of any material legal proceedings involving Altegris Funds or its principals in an adverse position to the Partnership or in which the Partnership has adverse interests.

1469317_11_ITEM5_P1_S0	As of February 28, 2011 the Partnership had 1,824 holders of Interests.

1469317_11_ITEM5_P2_S1	To date no distributions or dividends have been paid on the Interests, and Altegris Funds has no present intention to make any.

1469317_11_ITEM7_P0_S1	The information contained therein is essential to, and should be read in conjunction with, the following analysis.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P1_S0	The Partnership s assets are generally held as cash or cash equivalents, which are used to margin the Partnership s futures positions and are sold to pay redemptions and expenses as needed.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P1_S1	Other than any potential market-imposed limitations on liquidity, the Partnership s assets are highly liquid and are expected to remain so.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P1_S2	Market-imposed limitations, when they occur, can be due to limited open interest in certain futures markets or to daily price fluctuation limits, which are inherent in the Partnership s futures trading.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P2_S0	A portion of the Partnership s assets not used for margin and held with the Custodian are invested in liquid, high quality securities.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P2_S1	Through December 31, 2010 the Partnership experienced no meaningful periods of illiquidity in any of the markets traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P3_S0	The Partnership raises additional capital only through the sale of Interests and capital is increased through trading profits (if any) and interest income.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P3_S1	The Partnership does not engage in borrowing.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P4_S0	The amount of capital raised for the Partnership should not have a significant impact on its operations, as the Partnership has no significant capital expenditure or working capital requirements other than for capital to pay trading losses, brokerage commissions and expenses.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P4_S1	Within broad ranges of capitalization, the Partnership s trading positions should increase or decrease in approximate proportion to the size of the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P5_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts and may trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P5_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P5_S2	Further, the Partnership s FCMs and brokers may require margin in excess of minimum exchange requirements.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P6_S0	All of the futures contracts currently traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership are exchange-traded.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P6_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its trading counterparties, whereas exchange-traded contracts are generally, but not universally, backed by the collective credit of the members of the exchange.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P6_S2	In the future, the Partnership anticipates that it will enter into non-exchange-traded foreign currency contracts and be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P7_S0	The Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by Newedge USA and/or other clearing brokers or counterparties with which the Partnership trades.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P8_S0	The Partnership s success depends primarily upon QIM s ability to recognize and capitalize on market trends in the sectors of the global commodity futures markets in which it trades.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P8_S1	The Partnership seeks to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P8_S2	The past performance of the Partnership is not necessarily indicative of future results.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P9_S0	During 2010, the Partnership achieved net realized and unrealized gains of $275,424 from its trading of commodity futures contracts including brokerage commissions of $1,178,732.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P9_S1	The Partnership accrued net expenses of $2,520,021, including $375,888 in incentive fees, $904,887 in management fees paid to the General Partner, and $1,094,195 in service and professional fees.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P9_S2	The Partnership earned $340,113 in interest income during 2010.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P9_S3	An analysis of the profits and losses generated from the Partnership s commodity futures trading activities for each quarter during 2010 is set forth below.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P10_S0	The Partnership achieved a gain in October of 2010 as the Partnership exploited falling US Government debt yields which pushed the US Dollar lower against the Japanese yen.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P10_S1	Volatility in gold futures proved to be profitable for the Partnership during the month and soybean futures trading added significantly to the month s returns.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P10_S2	Trading in silver and natural gas futures also made a meaningful contribution to the gains achieved for the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P10_S3	The Partnership experienced a loss in November of 2010 as performance trailed off during the month s second and third weeks.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P10_S4	Corn and sugar futures accounted for the biggest gains in agricultural trading, as sugar hit a 30-year high during the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P10_S5	The Partnership later profited from a short position during a sharp sell-off of sugar.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P11_S0	After an excellent start to the month in crude oil futures trading, the Partnership suffered losses as crude oil made significant downward moves mid month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P11_S1	The Partnership experienced a gain in December with trading in stock index futures, interest rates and currencies contributing to profits.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P11_S2	Euro currency trading was profitable as the Partnership moved between long and short positions in the currency.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P11_S3	Futures trading in crude oil, equity indexes and bonds also yielded solid profits to help achieve gains during the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in July of 2010 due in large part to euro and Nasdaq and European stock index futures trading.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S1	The Partnership profited from its alternating long and short positions in the Nikkei and US equity index futures.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S2	Other profitable contracts included soybean futures as prices rose dramatically in the month s final three trading days on increased demand for soybeans.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S3	The Partnership achieved a gain in August of 2010 as the Partnership captured substantial gains in the interest rate and energy sectors.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S4	The Partnership capitalized on its positions in German interest rate futures as they set all-time price highs during the month with yields at record lows.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S5	The Partnership established a short position in crude oil futures as prices dropped on increased inventories.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S6	The Partnership achieved a gain in September of 2010 primarily on long positions in futures contracts on US stock indexes.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P12_S7	Trading in the longer-term US Treasury markets, contributed the bulk of gains in the interest rate sector during the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P13_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in April of 2010 amid strong sell-offs in the U.S. equity markets.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P13_S1	Short positions in futures contracts on the U.S. equity markets were profitable even though the month ended with performance down.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S0	The Partnership started the month strongly, spurred by long positions in gold, silver and copper contracts.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S1	The Partnership profited in the agricultural sector during the month, led by its trading of soybeans and sugar contracts, despite ending April negative.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S2	The Partnership experienced a loss in May of 2010.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S3	After beginning the month net short U.S. stock index futures, the Partnership spent the remainder of the month heavily tilted to the long side as the U.S. equity markets declined.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S4	The Partnership also suffered losses in Dax and yen trading despite gains in trading contracts on crude oil, the Euro and U.S. Government bonds.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S5	The Partnership achieved gains in June of 2010 with energy products driving performance during the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S6	A short position in crude oil futures benefitted from a decline in crude oil prices and a weaker-than-expected manufacturing report.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S7	The Partnership also held a profitable long position in natural gas futures throughout the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S8	Stock index futures trading generated positive returns as equity market volatilities retreated.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P14_S9	A positive month in metals trading was primarily attributable to continued increases in the price of gold which again reached an all-time high.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P15_S0	In January of 2010 the Partnership s performance was down with interest rate futures trading proving to be particularly difficult.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P15_S1	The Partnership held a strong, sector-wide, short bias during the first half of the month when prices in 11 out of 12 of the contracts traded rose substantially during the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P15_S2	The Partnership also suffered significant losses in Nikkei index futures, Australian dollar, Japanese yen, silver and crude oil contracts.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P16_S0	February saw the Partnership s performance fall slightly during the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P16_S1	The Partnership initially capitalized from its short positions as stock and commodity markets plummeted on troubling news of the Greek budget deficit, however, as the situation stabilized, the Partnership gave back those profits.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P17_S0	Short positions in stock index futures, crude oil and the euro drove returns early in the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P17_S1	Performance fell mid-month largely attributable to short positions in the metals, energies and agricultural commodities, particularly in the gold and crude oil markets.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P18_S0	The Partnership suffered through difficult trading early in March of 2010.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P18_S1	Performance began to stabilize during the second half of the month as the Partnership began to eke out positive returns.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P18_S2	Strong end of month performance in Nikkei index futures combined with solid month-long performance in U.S. equities index futures allowed for the sector to be slightly profitable, despite overall negative performance for the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P19_S0	The Partnership commenced operations on October 7, 2009.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P20_S0	During the fourth quarter of 2009, the Partnership achieved net realized and unrealized losses of $895,208 from its trading of commodity futures contracts including brokerage commissions of $65,454.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P20_S1	The Partnership accrued total expenses of $137,232, including $43,291 in management fees paid to the General Partner, and $83,792 in service and professional fees.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P20_S2	The Partnership earned $16,661 in interest income during 2009.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P20_S3	An analysis of the profits and losses generated from the Partnership s commodity futures trading activities for the fourth quarter of 2009 is set forth below.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P21_S0	The Partnership struggled through the end of October as major stock index futures sold off at month-end on the decline of equity markets.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P21_S1	After a very strong run on the long side of the equity markets, the Partnership initiated short positions during the month, but the equity markets did not start heading south until the Partnership was once again bullish.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P21_S2	Gold futures climbed to an all-time high and crude oil prices rose as the U.S. Dollar weakened.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P22_S0	The Partnership rebounded at the start of November as holdover equity positions, which had contributed to the prior month s drawdown, rallied during the first week.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P22_S1	At month-end, with the Partnership long, the Yen hit a 14-year high versus the U.S. Dollar.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P22_S2	The metals and agricultural sectors also provided meaningful boosts to the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P22_S3	Gold made up the bulk of gains in metals while gains in agricultural commodities were more evenly distributed across corn, soybeans and wheat trading.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P23_S0	The Partnership was down for the month of December, struggling through particularly difficult market conditions at the beginning of the month.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P23_S1	The Partnership s long positions in foreign currencies dropped as the U.S. Dollar reacted strongly to better than expected U.S. employment numbers.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P23_S2	The Partnership s interest rate trading also suffered as rates reacted strongly to the employment report.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P23_S3	Interest rate futures contributed positively, but gold trading experienced losses.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P24_S0	The Partnership does not engage in off-balance sheet arrangements with other entities.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P25_S0	Altegris Funds believes that the Partnership s most critical accounting estimates relate to the valuation of the Partnership s assets.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P26_S0	Futures and options on futures contracts are valued using the primary exchange s closing price.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P26_S1	Forward currency contracts are stated at fair value using spot currency rates provided by Newedge USA, LLC and adjusted for interest rates and other typical adjustment factors.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P27_S0	United States government agency securities are generally valued based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P27_S1	Corporate notes and repurchase agreements are generally valued at cost given their short duration from the time of purchase.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P28_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P28_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P29_S0	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the statement of financial condition.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P29_S1	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_11_ITEM7_P29_S2	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in income currently.

1469317_11_ITEM11_P0_S3	Altegris Funds receives a monthly management fee equal to 1/12 of 1.25% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Class A and Class B Interests and equal to 1/12 of 0.75% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Institutional Interests.
1469317_11_ITEM11_P0_S4	Altegris Funds also receives a monthly administrative fee equal to 1/12 of 0.333% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Class A and Class B Interests.

1469317_11_ITEM11_P3_S0	The Partnership will pay monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_11_ITEM11_P3_S1	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_11_ITEM11_P3_S2	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay only the amount described in (A) above.

1469317_11_ITEM15_P16_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. ( Partnership ) (formerly APM QIM Futures Fund, L.P.) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P16_S1	The Partnership speculatively trades commodity futures contracts, and may trade options on futures contracts, forward contracts and other commodity interests.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P17_S0	The objective of the Partnership s business is appreciation of its assets.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P17_S1	It is subject to the regulations of the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (the CFTC ), an agency of the United States ( U.S. ) Government which regulates most aspects of the commodity futures industry; rules of the National Futures Association, an industry self-regulatory organization; and the requirements of commodity exchanges and Futures Commission Merchants (brokers) through which the Partnership trades.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P18_S0	The Partnership follows accounting standards set by the Financial Accounting Standards Board, commonly referred to as the FASB.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P18_S1	The FASB sets generally accepted accounting principles ( GAAP ) that the Partnership follows to ensure consistent reporting of the Partnership s financial condition, results of operations, and changes in partners capital.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P18_S2	References to GAAP issued by the FASB in these footnotes are to the FASB Accounting Standards Codification referred to as ASC .
1469317_11_ITEM15_P18_S3	The FASB finalized the ASC effective for periods ending on or after September 15, 2009.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P19_S0	The Partnership s financial statements are presented in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America, which require the use of certain estimates made by the Partnership s management.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P19_S1	Actual results could differ from those estimates.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P20_S0	Pursuant to the Cash Flows Topic of the Codification, the Partnership qualifies for an exemption from the requirement to provide a statement of cash flows and has elected not to provide a statement of cash flows.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P21_S0	Cash and cash equivalents includes cash and other highly liquid investments with financial institutions with original maturity dates of 90 days or less.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P22_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P22_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P22_S2	Any change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the statement of operations.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P23_S0	Brokerage commissions and other trading fees are reflected as an adjustment to cost or proceeds at the time of the transaction.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P23_S1	Interest income is recorded on the accrual basis.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P24_S0	Gains or losses on futures contracts and options on futures contracts are realized when contracts are liquidated.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P24_S1	Net unrealized gains or losses on open contracts (the difference between contract trade price and quoted market price) are reflected in the statement of financial condition.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P24_S2	Any change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the statement of operations.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P25_S0	Brokerage commissions on futures and options on futures contracts include other trading fees and are charged to expense when contracts are opened.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P26_S0	The Partnership values its investments in accordance with Accounting Standards Codification 820 - Fair Value Measurements ( ASC 820 ).
1469317_11_ITEM15_P26_S1	Under ASC 820, fair value is defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability (i.e., the exit price ) in an orderly transaction between market participants at the measurement date.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P27_S0	In determining fair value, the Partnership uses various valuation approaches.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P28_S0	ASC 820 establishes a fair value hierarchy for inputs used in measuring fair value that maximizes the use of observable inputs and minimizes the use of unobservable inputs by requiring that the most observable inputs be used when available.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P29_S0	Observable inputs are those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability based on market data obtained from sources independent of the Partnership.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P30_S0	Unobservable inputs reflect the Partnership s assumption about the inputs market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability developed based on the best information available in the circumstances.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P30_S1	The fair value hierarchy is categorized into three levels based on the inputs as follows:
1469317_11_ITEM15_P31_S0	Level 1 - Valuations based on unadjusted quoted prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities that the Partnership has the ability to access.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P31_S1	Valuation adjustments and blockage discounts are not applied to Level 1 assets and liabilities.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P32_S0	Because valuations are based on quoted prices that are readily and regularly available in an active market, valuation of these assets and liabilities does not entail a significant degree of judgment.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P33_S0	Level 2 - Valuations based on quoted prices in markets that are not active or for which all significant inputs are observable, either directly or indirectly.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P34_S0	Level 3 - Valuations based on inputs that are unobservable and significant to the overall fair value measurement.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P35_S0	The availability of valuation techniques and observable inputs can vary among assets and liabilities and is affected by a wide variety of factors, including the type of asset or liability, whether the asset or liability is new and not yet established in the marketplace, and other characteristics particular to the transaction.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P36_S0	To the extent that valuation is based on models or inputs that are less observable or unobservable in the market, the determination of fair value requires more judgment.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P36_S1	Those estimated values do not necessarily represent the amounts that may be ultimately realized due to the occurrence of future circumstances that cannot be reasonably determined.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P36_S2	Because of the inherent uncertainty of valuation, those estimated values may be materially higher or lower than the values that would have been used had a ready market for the asset or liability existed.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P36_S3	Accordingly, the degree of judgment exercised by the Partnership in determining fair value is greatest for assets and liabilities categorized in Level 3.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P37_S0	In certain cases, the inputs used to measure fair value may fall into different levels of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P37_S1	In such cases, for disclosure purposes, the level in the fair value hierarchy within which the fair value measurement falls in its entirety is determined by the lowest level input that is significant to the fair value measurement.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P38_S0	Fair value is a market-based measure considered from the perspective of a market participant rather than an entity-specific measure.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P38_S1	Therefore, even when market assumptions are not readily available, the Partnership s own assumptions are set to reflect those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability at the measurement date.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P39_S0	The Partnership uses prices and inputs that are current as of the measurement date, including during periods of market dislocation.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P39_S1	In periods of market dislocation, the observability of prices and inputs may be reduced for many assets and liabilities.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P39_S2	This condition could cause an asset or liability to be reclassified to a lower level within the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P40_S0	The Partnership values futures and options on futures contracts at the closing price of the contract s primary exchange.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P41_S0	The Partnership includes futures and options on futures contracts in Level 1 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P42_S0	The fair value of U.S. Government bonds is generally based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P42_S1	When quoted prices are not available, fair value is determined based on a valuation model that uses inputs that include interest-rate yield curves, cross-currency-basis index spreads, and country credit spreads similar to the bond in terms of issue, maturity and seniority.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P43_S0	U.S. Government bonds are generally categorized in Levels 1 or 2 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P44_S0	The fair value of corporate bonds is estimated using recently executed transactions, market price quotations (where observable), bond spreads or credit default swap spreads.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P44_S1	The spread data used are for the same maturity as of the bond.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P44_S2	If the spread data does not reference the issuer, then data that references a comparable issuer is used.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P45_S0	When observable price quotations are not available, fair value is determined based on cash flow models with yield curves, bond, or single-name credit default swap spreads and recovery rates based on collateral values as key inputs.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P45_S1	These valuation methods represent both a market and income approach to fair value measurement.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P46_S0	Corporate bonds are generally categorized in Level 2 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P46_S1	In instances where significant inputs are unobservable, they are categorized in Level 3 of the hierarchy.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P47_S0	The industry classifications included in the condensed schedule of investments represent the General Partner s belief as to the most meaningful presentation of the classification of the Partnership s investments.

1469317_11_ITEM15_P57_S1	This accounting standard requires the evaluation of tax positions taken or expected to be taken in the course of preparing the Partnership s financial statements to determine whether the tax positions are more-likely-than-not of being sustained by the applicable tax authority.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P57_S2	Tax positions with respect to tax at the Partnership level not deemed to meet the more-likely-than-not threshold would be recorded as an expense in the current year.

1469317_11_ITEM15_P65_S0	Improving Disclosures about Fair Value Measurements .
1469317_11_ITEM15_P65_S1	ASU 2010-06 amends the Fair Value Measurements and Disclosures Topic of the Codification to add new disclosure requirements about transfers into and out of Levels 1 and 2 and separate disclosures about purchases, sales, issuances and settlements in the reconciliation for fair value measurements using significant unobservable inputs (Level 3).
1469317_11_ITEM15_P65_S2	It also clarifies existing disclosure requirements relating to the levels of disaggregation for fair value measurement and inputs and valuation techniques used to measure fair value.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P65_S3	ASU 2010-06 is effective for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2009, except for disclosures about purchases, sales, issuances, and settlements in the roll forward of activity in Level 3 fair value measurements, which are effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2010, and for interim periods within those fiscal years.

1469317_11_ITEM15_P79_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P79_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P79_S2	Further, the Clearing Broker has the right to require margin in excess of the minimum exchange requirement.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P79_S3	Risk arises from changes in the value of these contracts (market risk) and the potential inability of brokers to perform under the terms of their contracts (credit risk).
1469317_11_ITEM15_P80_S0	All of the contracts currently traded by the Partnership are exchange traded.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P80_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its respective individual counterparties.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P80_S2	However if, in the future, the Partnership were to enter into non-exchange traded contracts, it would be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P80_S3	The credit risk from counterparty non-performance associated with such instruments is the net unrealized gain, if any.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P81_S0	The Partnership also has credit risk because the sole counterparty to all domestic futures contracts is the exchange clearing corporation.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P81_S1	In addition, the Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by the Clearing Broker.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P82_S0	The Partnership s policy is to continuously monitor its exposure to market and counterparty risk through the use of a variety of financial, position and credit exposure reporting and control procedures.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P82_S1	In addition, the Partnership has a policy of reviewing the credit standing of each clearing broker or counterparty with which it conducts business.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P83_S0	The Partnership has cash deposited with Wilmington Trust Company ( Custodian ).
1469317_11_ITEM15_P83_S1	For cash not held with the Clearing Broker, the Partnership receives cash management services from an affiliate of the Custodian, Wilmington Trust Investment Management ( WTIM ).
1469317_11_ITEM15_P83_S2	The Partnership has a substantial portion of its assets on deposit with WTIM in U.S. Government agency bonds and notes and corporate notes.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P84_S0	Risks arise from investments in bonds and notes due to possible illiquidity and the potential for default by the issuer or counterparty.
1469317_11_ITEM15_P84_S1	Such instruments are also sensitive to changes in interest rates and economic conditions.

1469317_11_ITEM15_P85_S2	The Partnership expects the risk of any future obligation under these indemnifications to be remote.

(d/b/a Altegris Funds), an Arkansas corporation ( Altegris Funds or the General Partner ), serves as general partner of the Partnership and has sole responsibility for management and administration of all aspects of the Partnership s business.

1469317_12_ITEM1_P5_S0	The Partnership is not required to be, and is not, registered under the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P6_S0	As of February 29, 2012, the aggregate net asset value of the Interests in the Partnership before redemptions was $118,884,093.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P6_S1	The Partnership operates on a calendar fiscal year and has no subsidiaries.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P7_S0	The Partnership offers three classes of Interests: Class A, Class B and Institutional Interests (each, a Class of Interest ).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P7_S1	The Classes of Interests differ from each other only in the fees that they pay and the applicable investment minimums.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P8_S0	The Partnership s business constitutes only one segment for financial reporting purposes i.e. , a speculative commodity pool.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P8_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P8_S2	Financial information regarding the Partnership s business is set forth in the Partnership s financial statements, included herewith.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P9_S0	The Partnership s objective is to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P10_S0	QIM believes that financial markets are not entirely efficient and that numerous small inefficiencies exist and can be exploited through the prudent use of robust analysis and predictive technologies.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P11_S0	QIM currently employs several thousand quantitative trading models that utilize pattern recognition to predict short-term price movements in global futures markets.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P11_S1	All models are tested across large data sets that expose them to a wide range of market, economic, and political environments, as well as a wide range of time frames and interactions.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P11_S2	Only those models that prove to be the most robust, statistically significant, and conceptually diverse are used in actual trading.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P11_S3	The resultant system of models offers what QIM believes to be reliable signals that guide market timing and trade allocation.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P12_S0	QIM s trading strategies and models may be revised from time to time as a result of ongoing research and development seeking to devise new strategies and systems as well as to improve current methods.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P12_S1	The strategies and systems used by QIM in the future may differ significantly from those currently in use due to changes resulting from this research, and Limited Partners will not be informed of these changes as they may occur.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P13_S0	QIM applies risk management procedures that take into account the price, size, volatility, liquidity, and inter-relationships of the contracts traded.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P13_S1	The Partnership s positions are generally balanced in a manner that allocates approximately equal amounts of measured risk to as many distinct markets as possible and during significant drawdowns in equity, QIM will reduce market exposure by scaling back the Partnership s overall leverage.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P14_S0	QIM s trading is generally approximately 95% systematic and 5% discretionary.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P14_S1	All facets of the predictive models, risk management, and trade allocation are fully automated or proceduralized.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P14_S2	In this sense, the trading is systematic.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P14_S3	Discretion of QIM, however, plays a significant role in the pursuit of improvements to the Program.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P15_S0	QIM has different time horizons for the execution of certain trades.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P15_S1	For example, QIM may have certain trades executed at the beginning of the trading day while giving the executing broker limited discretion with respect to other trades.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P16_S0	QIM currently trades or monitors over 50 tradable markets in currencies, stock indices, interest rates, energy, grains, softs and metals.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P16_S1	QIM may add or delete markets from this universe of tradable markets in its discretion if QIM s research demonstrates that such an addition or deletion would enhance the program s performance.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P17_S0	All markets are futures markets or interbank currency markets.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P18_S0	QIM seeks to profitably trade each of these markets while taking advantage of the diversification available from such a varied universe of futures contracts.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P18_S1	QIM s trading program often takes opposing long and short positions within the same or related classes of correlated futures, which, taken in conjunction with the effect of diversification across a broad range of contracts, generally results in reduced market exposure than trading a single market with similar leverage.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P19_S0	A substantial portion of the equity in the Partnership s account is invested in United States ( U.S. ) government and agency securities and other liquid, high-quality instruments at the direction of the Custodian (as defined below).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P19_S1	QIM will target an average margin to equity level of between 4% and 18%.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P19_S2	The actual percentage of assets committed to margin at any time may be higher or lower than the target level.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P20_S0	and available for trading by QIM in Commodity Interests on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P20_S1	Interest on Partnership assets held at Newedge USA in cash or Treasury securities will be credited to the Partnership as described under Charges.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P20_S2	Depending on market factors, the amount of margin or option premiums held at Newedge USA could change significantly, and all of the Partnership s assets are available for use as margin.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P20_S3	The Partnership may also retain other brokers and/or dealers from time to time to clear or execute a portion of Partnership trades made by QIM.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P21_S0	With respect to Partnership assets not held at Newedge USA as described above, but deposited with JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A. (the Custodian ), the portion not held in checking, money market or other bank accounts (and used to pay Partnership operating expenses) will be invested in liquid, high-quality short-term securities at the direction of the Custodian or its affiliate, J.P. Morgan Investment Management Inc. ( JPMIM ).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P21_S1	The Partnership s custody and investment management agreement with the Custodian permits the Custodian to invest in U.S. government and agency securities, other securities or instruments guaranteed by the U.S. government or its agencies, CDs, time deposits, banker s acceptances, commercial paper and repurchase agreements subject in each case to specific diversification, credit quality and maturity limitations.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P21_S2	The Custodian may use sub-advisers to attempt to increase yield enhancement.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P21_S3	The General Partner may direct that a portion of Partnership assets be deposited with other custodians and retain other sub-advisers for the purpose of attempting to increase yield enhancement via other cash management arrangements.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P22_S0	The percentage of the Partnership s assets deposited with these firms is also subject to change in the General Partner s sole discretion.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P22_S1	The Partnership s assets will not be commingled with the assets of any other person.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P22_S2	Depositing the Partnership s assets with banks or Newedge USA, or other clearing brokers, as segregated funds is not commingling for these purposes.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P23_S0	The Partnership pays all of its ongoing liabilities, expenses and costs.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P24_S0	Altegris Funds receives a management fee of 0.104% of the month-end net asset value, before deduction for any accrued incentive fees related to the current quarter (the management fee net asset value ), of all Class A Interests (1.25% per annum), 0.104% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Class B Interests (1.25% per annum) and 0.0625% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Institutional Interests (0.75% per annum).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P24_S1	QIM receives a 30% of quarterly trading profits applicable to each Class of Interest.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P25_S0	Each selling agent selling Class A Interests receives 0.166% of the month-end net asset value of the Partnership apportioned to each Class A Interest sold by such selling agent (2% per annum) and may elect to receive 0.0417% of the month-end net asset value apportioned to any Institutional Interest sold by such selling (0.50% per annum).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P26_S0	Newedge USA paid Altegris during 2011 and will pay Altegris Futures from and after January 1, 2012 a portion of the brokerage commissions and transaction fees received from the Partnership as well as a portion of the interest income received on the Partnership s assets.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P27_S0	Monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P27_S1	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P27_S2	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership pays only the amount described in (A) above.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P28_S0	The Partnership generally pays its operating expenses as they are incurred.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P28_S1	However, during the first twelve months after the Partnership commenced trading, the General Partner agreed to limit the operating expenses paid by the Partnership to 1/12 th of 0.5% of the month-end capital account balances of all Interests for such month.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P29_S0	A fixed administrative fee is charged to Class A and Class B Interests and paid to Altegris Funds equal to 0.0275% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balance of all such Class A and Class B Interests (0.333% per annum).
1469317_12_ITEM1_P30_S0	The CFTC has delegated to NFA responsibility for the registration of commodity trading advisors, commodity pool operators, futures commission merchants, introducing brokers and their respective associated persons and floor brokers and floor traders.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S0	The Commodity Exchange Act requires commodity pool operators such as Altegris Funds, commodity trading advisors such as QIM and commodity brokers or FCMs such as Newedge USA and introducing brokers such as Altegris Futures to be registered and to comply with various reporting and record keeping requirements.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S1	CFTC regulations also require FCMs and certain introducing brokers to maintain a minimum level of net capital.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S2	In addition, the CFTC and certain commodities exchanges have established limits referred to as speculative position limits on the maximum net long or net short speculative positions that any person may hold or control in any particular futures or options contracts traded on U.S. commodities exchanges.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S3	All accounts owned or managed by QIM will be combined for position limit purposes.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S4	QIM could be required to liquidate positions held for the Partnership in order to comply with such limits.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S5	Any such liquidation could result in substantial costs to the Partnership.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P31_S6	In addition, many futures exchanges impose limits beyond which the price of a futures contract may not trade during the course of a trading day, and there is a potential for a futures contract to hit its daily price limit for several days in a row, making it impossible for QIM to liquidate a position and thereby experiencing a dramatic loss.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P32_S0	Currency forward contracts currently are not subject to regulation by any U.S. government agency.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P33_S0	In addition to such registration requirements, the CFTC and certain commodity exchanges have established limits on the maximum net long or net short position which any person may hold or control in particular commodities.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P33_S1	Most exchanges also limit the changes in futures contract prices that may occur during a single trading day.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P34_S0	In January 2011, the CFTC proposed a separate position limits regime for 28 so-called exempt (i.e. metals and energy) and agricultural futures and options contracts and their economically equivalent swap contracts.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P34_S1	Position limits in spot months are proposed to be 25% of the official estimated deliverable supply of the underlying commodity and in a non-spot month a percentage of the average aggregate 12-month rolling open interest in all months (swaps and futures) for each contract.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P34_S2	The General Partner believes that the proposed limits are sufficiently large that if adopted, they should not restrict the Partnership s trading strategy.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P35_S0	Currency forward contracts are not currently subject to regulation by any U.S. Government agency.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P36_S0	The Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act (the Reform Act ) was enacted in July 2010.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P36_S1	The Reform Act includes provisions that comprehensively regulate the over-the-counter derivatives markets for the first time.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P36_S2	The Reform Act will mandate that a substantial portion of over-the-counter derivatives must be executed in regulated markets and submitted for clearing to regulated clearinghouses.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P36_S3	The mandates imposed by the Reform Act may result in the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees with respect to any swaps entered into by the Partnership.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P37_S0	The Reform Act also amended the definition of eligible contract participant, and the CFTC may interpret that definition in such a manner that the Partnership may no longer be permitted to engage in forward currency transactions by directly accessing the interbank market.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P37_S1	If is does so (final rules are still pending), the Partnership may be limited to engaging in retail forex transactions which could limit the Partnership s potential forward currency counterparties to futures commission merchants and retail foreign exchange dealers.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P37_S2	Limiting on the Partnership s potential forward currency counterparties in this manner could lead to the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P37_S3	The retail forex markets could also be significantly less liquid than the interbank market.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P37_S4	Moreover, the creditworthiness of the futures commission merchants and retail foreign exchange dealers with which the Partnership may be required to trade could be significantly weaker than the creditworthiness of the financial institutions with which the Partnership currently engages for its forward currency transactions.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P37_S5	Although the impact of requiring the Partnership to conduct forward currency transactions in the retail market could be substantial, the full scope is currently unknown and the ultimate effect could also be negligible.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P38_S0	The Partnership has no operations in foreign countries although it trades on foreign exchanges and other non-U.S. markets.
1469317_12_ITEM1_P38_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.

1469317_12_ITEM7_P1_S1	Other than any potential market-imposed limitations on liquidity, the Partnership s assets are highly liquid and are expected to remain so.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P1_S2	Market-imposed limitations, when they occur, can be due to limited open interest in certain futures markets or to daily price fluctuation limits, which are inherent in the Partnership s futures trading.

1469317_12_ITEM7_P3_S1	The Partnership does not engage in borrowing.

1469317_12_ITEM7_P4_S1	Within broad ranges of capitalization, the Partnership s trading positions should increase or decrease in approximate proportion to the size of the Partnership.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P5_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts and may trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P5_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P5_S2	Further, the Partnership s FCMs and brokers may require margin in excess of minimum exchange requirements.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P6_S0	All of the futures contracts currently traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership are exchange-traded.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P6_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its trading counterparties, whereas exchange-traded contracts are generally, but not universally, backed by the collective credit of the members of the exchange.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P6_S2	In the future, the Partnership anticipates that it will enter into non-exchange-traded foreign currency contracts and be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P7_S0	The Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by Newedge USA and/or other clearing brokers or counterparties with which the Partnership trades.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P8_S0	The Partnership s success depends primarily upon QIM s ability to recognize and capitalize on market trends in the sectors of the global commodity futures markets in which it trades.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P8_S1	The Partnership seeks to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.

1469317_12_ITEM7_P20_S2	Euro currency trading was profitable as the Partnership moved between long and short positions in the currency.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P20_S3	Futures trading in crude oil, equity indexes and bonds also yielded solid profits to help achieve gains during the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in July of 2010 due in large part to euro and Nasdaq and European stock index futures trading.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S1	The Partnership profited from its alternating long and short positions in the Nikkei and US equity index futures.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S2	Other profitable contracts included soybean futures as prices rose dramatically in the month s final three trading days on increased demand for soybeans.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S3	The Partnership achieved a gain in August of 2010 as the Partnership captured substantial gains in the interest rate and energy sectors.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S4	The Partnership capitalized on its positions in German interest rate futures as they set all-time price highs during the month with yields at record lows.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S5	The Partnership established a short position in crude oil futures as prices dropped on increased inventories.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S6	The Partnership achieved a gain in September of 2010 primarily on long positions in futures contracts on US stock indexes.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P21_S7	Trading in the longer-term US Treasury markets, contributed the bulk of gains in the interest rate sector during the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P22_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in April of 2010 amid strong sell-offs in the U.S. equity markets.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P22_S1	Short positions in futures contracts on the U.S. equity markets were profitable even though the month ended with performance down.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S0	The Partnership started the month strongly, spurred by long positions in gold, silver and copper contracts.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S1	The Partnership profited in the agricultural sector during the month, led by its trading of soybeans and sugar contracts, despite ending April negative.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S2	The Partnership experienced a loss in May of 2010.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S3	After beginning the month net short U.S. stock index futures, the Partnership spent the remainder of the month heavily tilted to the long side as the U.S. equity markets declined.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S4	The Partnership also suffered losses in Dax and yen trading despite gains in trading contracts on crude oil, the Euro and U.S. Government bonds.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S5	The Partnership achieved gains in June of 2010 with energy products driving performance during the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S6	A short position in crude oil futures benefitted from a decline in crude oil prices and a weaker-than-expected manufacturing report.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S7	The Partnership also held a profitable long position in natural gas futures throughout the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S8	Stock index futures trading generated positive returns as equity market volatilities retreated.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P23_S9	A positive month in metals trading was primarily attributable to continued increases in the price of gold which again reached an all-time high.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P24_S0	In January of 2010 the Partnership s performance was down with interest rate futures trading proving to be particularly difficult.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P24_S1	The Partnership held a strong, sector-wide, short bias during the first half of the month when prices in 11 out of 12 of the contracts traded rose substantially during the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P24_S2	The Partnership also suffered significant losses in Nikkei index futures, Australian dollar, Japanese yen, silver and crude oil contracts.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P25_S0	February saw the Partnership s performance fall slightly during the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P25_S1	The Partnership initially capitalized from its short positions as stock and commodity markets plummeted on troubling news of the Greek budget deficit, however, as the situation stabilized, the Partnership gave back those profits.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P26_S0	Short positions in stock index futures, crude oil and the euro drove returns early in the month.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P26_S1	Performance fell mid-month largely attributable to short positions in the metals, energies and agricultural commodities, particularly in the gold and crude oil markets.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P27_S0	The Partnership suffered through difficult trading early in March of 2010.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P27_S1	Performance began to stabilize during the second half of the month as the Partnership began to eke out positive returns.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P27_S2	Strong end of month performance in Nikkei index futures combined with solid month-long performance in U.S. equities index futures allowed for the sector to be slightly profitable, despite overall negative performance for the month.

1469317_12_ITEM7_P32_S0	The Partnership does not engage in off-balance sheet arrangements with other entities.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P33_S0	Altegris Funds believes that the Partnership s most critical accounting estimates relate to the valuation of the Partnership s assets.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P34_S0	Futures and options on futures contracts are valued using the primary exchange s closing price.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P34_S1	Forward currency contracts are stated at fair value using spot currency rates provided by Newedge USA, LLC and adjusted for interest rates and other typical adjustment factors.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P35_S0	U.S. government agency securities are generally valued based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P35_S1	Corporate notes and repurchase agreements are generally valued at fair value, which usually approximates cost, given their short duration from the time of purchase.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P36_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P36_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P37_S0	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the statement of financial condition.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P37_S1	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_12_ITEM7_P37_S2	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in income currently.

1469317_12_ITEM7_P38_S3	The estimates used do not provide a range of possible results that would require the exercise of subjective judgment.

1469317_12_ITEM9A_P1_S0	Altegris Funds, the general partner of the Partnership is responsible for the management of the Partnership.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management of Altegris Funds ( Management ) is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P2_S1	The internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P3_S0	Provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or disposition of the Partnership s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P4_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P4_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P5_S0	Management assessed the effectiveness of the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting as of December 31, 2011.
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P5_S1	In making this assessment, Management used the criteria set forth in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission ( COSO ).
1469317_12_ITEM9A_P5_S2	As a result of this assessment and based on the criteria in the COSO framework, management has concluded that, as of December 31, 2011, the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting was effective.
