1469317_12_ITEM11_P0_S2	All persons serving in the capacity of officers or executives of Altegris Funds, the General Partner of the Partnership, are compensated by Altegris, a wholly-owned subsidiary of Genworth Financial, Inc. as of December 31, 2010 and/or an affiliate in respect of their respective positions with such entities.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P0_S3	Altegris Funds receives a monthly management fee equal to 1/12 of 1.25% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Class A and Class B Interests and equal to 1/12 of 0.75% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Institutional Interests.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P0_S4	Altegris Funds also receives a monthly administrative fee equal to 1/12 of 0.333% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Class A and Class B Interests.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P1_S0	Altegris receives continuing monthly compensation from the Partnership equal to 1/12 of 2% of the month-end net asset value of Class A Interests sold by Altegris.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P2_S0	From January 1, 2011, Altegris Futures, in its capacity as Introducing Broker to the Partnership, received compensation for brokerage-related services.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P2_S1	The Partnership will pay monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_12_ITEM11_P2_S2	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P2_S3	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay only the amount described in (A) above.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P3_S0	The Partnership has no other compensation arrangements.
1469317_12_ITEM11_P3_S1	There are no compensation plans or arrangements relating to a change in control of the Partnership.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P11_S0	We have audited the statement of financial condition of Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. as of December 31, 2011, and the related statements of operations and changes in partners capital for the year then ended.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P11_S1	These financial statements are the responsibility of the Partnership's management.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P11_S2	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audit.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P11_S3	The financial statements of Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. for the year and period ended December 31, 2010 and October 7, 2009 through December 31, 2009, respectively, were audited by other auditors whose report dated March 25, 2011, expressed an unqualified opinion on those statements.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P12_S0	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P12_S1	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P12_S2	We were not engaged to perform an audit of the Company's internal control over financial reporting.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P12_S3	Our audits included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company's internal control over financial reporting.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P12_S4	Accordingly, we express no such opinion.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P13_S1	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P14_S0	In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. at December 31, 2011, and the results of its operations, and changes in partners capital for the year ended December 31, 2011, in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P15_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. ( Partnership ) (formerly APM QIM Futures Fund, L.P.) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P15_S1	The Partnership's general partner is Altegris Portfolio Management, Inc. (d/b/a Altegris Funds) ("General Partner").
1469317_12_ITEM15_P16_S0	The Partnership speculatively trades commodity futures contracts, and may trade options on futures contracts, forward contracts and other commodity interests.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P17_S0	The objective of the Partnership s business is appreciation of its assets.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P17_S1	It is subject to the regulations of the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (the CFTC ), an agency of the U.S. Government which regulates most aspects of the commodity futures industry; rules of the National Futures Association, an industry self-regulatory organization; and the requirements of commodity exchanges and Futures Commission Merchants (brokers) through which the Partnership trades.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P18_S0	The Partnership s financial statements are presented in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles ( U.S. GAAP ).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P18_S1	The preparation of the financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported fair value of assets and liabilities, disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities as of December 31, 2011 and 2010 and for the period October 7, 2009 (inception of trading) to December 31, 2009, and reported amounts of income and expenses for the years and period then ended.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P18_S2	Management believes that the estimates utilized in preparing the Partnership s financial statements are reasonable, however, actual results could differ from these estimates and it is reasonably possible that differences could be material.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P19_S0	In accordance with the authoritative guidance under U.S. GAAP, fair value is defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability (i.e., the exit price ) in an orderly transaction between market participants at the measurement date.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P20_S0	In determining fair value, the Partnership uses various valuation approaches.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P21_S0	The authoritative guidance under U.S. GAAP establishes a fair value hierarchy for inputs used in measuring fair value that maximizes the use of observable inputs and minimizes the use of unobservable inputs by requiring that the most observable inputs be used when available.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P22_S0	Observable inputs are those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability based on market data obtained from sources independent of the Partnership.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P23_S0	Unobservable inputs reflect the Partnership s assumption about the inputs market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability developed based on the best information available in the circumstances.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P23_S1	The fair value hierarchy is categorized into three levels based on the inputs as follows:
1469317_12_ITEM15_P24_S0	Level 1 - Valuations based on unadjusted quoted prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities that the Partnership has the ability to access.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P25_S0	Level 2 - Valuations based on quoted prices in markets that are not active or for which all significant inputs are observable, either directly or indirectly.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P26_S0	Level 3 - Valuations based on inputs that are unobservable.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P27_S0	The availability of valuation techniques and observable inputs can vary among assets and liabilities and is affected by a wide variety of factors, including the type of asset or liability, whether the asset or liability is new and not yet established in the marketplace, and other characteristics particular to the transaction.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P28_S0	To the extent that valuation is based on models or inputs that are less observable or unobservable in the market, the determination of fair value requires more judgment.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P28_S1	Those estimated values do not necessarily represent the amounts that may be ultimately realized due to the occurrence of future circumstances that cannot be reasonably determined.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P28_S2	Because of the inherent uncertainty of valuation, those estimated values may be materially higher or lower than the values that would have been used had a ready market for the asset or liability existed.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P28_S3	Accordingly, the degree of judgment exercised by the Partnership in determining fair value is greatest for assets and liabilities categorized in Level 3.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P29_S0	In certain cases, the inputs used to measure fair value may fall into different levels of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P29_S1	In such cases, for disclosure purposes, the level in the fair value hierarchy within which the fair value measurement falls in its entirety is determined by the lowest level input that is significant to the fair value measurement.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P30_S0	Fair value is a market-based measure considered from the perspective of a market participant rather than an entity-specific measure.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P30_S1	Therefore, even when market assumptions are not readily available, the Partnership s own assumptions are set to reflect those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability at the measurement date.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P31_S0	The Partnership uses prices and inputs that are current as of the measurement date, including during periods of market dislocation.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P31_S1	In periods of market dislocation, the observability of prices and inputs may be reduced for many assets and liabilities.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P31_S2	This condition could cause an asset or liability to be reclassified to a lower level within the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P32_S0	The Partnership values futures and options on futures contracts at the closing price of the contract s primary exchange.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P33_S0	The Partnership includes futures and options on futures contracts in Level 1 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P34_S0	The fair value of U.S. Government agency bonds and notes is generally based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P34_S1	When quoted prices are not available, fair value is determined based on a valuation model that uses inputs that include interest-rate yield curves, cross-currency-basis index spreads, and country credit spreads similar to the bond in terms of issue, maturity and seniority.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P35_S0	U.S. Government agency bonds and notes are generally categorized in Levels 1 or 2 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P35_S1	There were no fair value U.S. Government agency bonds and notes at December 31, 2011 and 2010.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P36_S0	The fair value of corporate notes is estimated using recently executed transactions, market price quotations (where observable), notes spreads or credit default swap spreads.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P36_S1	The spread data used are for the same maturity as of the notes.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P36_S2	If the spread data does not reference the issuer, then data that references a comparable issuer is used.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P37_S0	When observable price quotations are not available, fair value is determined based on cash flow models with yield curves, notes, or single-name credit default swap spreads and recovery rates based on collateral values as key inputs.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P37_S1	These valuation methods represent both a market and income approach to fair value measurement.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P38_S0	Corporate notes are generally categorized in Level 2 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P38_S1	In instances where significant inputs are unobservable, they are categorized in Level 3 of the hierarchy.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P39_S0	There were no fair value corporate notes at December 31, 2011 and 2010.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P40_S0	The inputs or methodology used for valuing securities are not necessarily an indication of the risk associated with investing in those securities.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P40_S1	There were no changes in the Fund s valuation methodology during the years ended December 31, 2011 and 2010.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P42_S0	"Financial Derivative Instruments" for the fair value in each type of contracts within this category.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P43_S0	For the years ended December 31, 2011 and 2010, there were no transfers between Level 1 and Level 2 assets and liabilities.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P44_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P44_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P44_S2	Change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the statement of operations.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P45_S0	Brokerage commissions and other trading fees are reflected as an adjustment to cost or proceeds at the time of the transaction.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P45_S1	Interest income is recorded on the accrual basis.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P46_S0	Gains or losses on futures contracts and options on futures contracts are realized when contracts are liquidated.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P46_S1	Net unrealized gains or losses on open contracts (the difference between contract trade price and quoted market price) are reflected in the statement of financial condition.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P46_S2	Any change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the statement of operations.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P47_S0	Brokerage commissions on futures and options on futures contracts include other trading fees and are charged to expense when contracts are opened.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P48_S0	The Partnership may engage in futures contracts as part of its investment strategy to hedge against changes in the value of its portfolio securities and in the value of securities it intends to purchase.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P49_S0	Upon entering into a futures contract, the Partnership is required to deposit with the broker an amount of cash or cash equivalents equal to a certain percentage of the contract amount.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P49_S1	This is known as the initial margin.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P49_S2	Subsequent payments ( variation margin ) are made or received by the Partnership each day, depending on the daily fluctuations in the value of the contract, and are included in unrealized appreciation/depreciation on futures contracts.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P50_S0	The Partnership recognizes a realized gain or loss when the contract is closed.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P51_S0	There are several risks in connection with the use of futures contracts as an investment option.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P51_S1	The change in value of futures contracts primarily corresponds with the value of their underlying instruments, which may not correlate with the change in value of the investments that are intended to hedge against.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P51_S2	In addition, there is the risk that the Partnership may not be able to enter into a closing transaction because of an illiquid secondary market.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P52_S0	Open positions in futures contracts at December 31, 2011 are reflected within the Condensed Schedule of Investments.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P53_S0	The Partnership s functional currency is the U.S. dollar; however, it transacts business in currencies other than the U.S. dollar.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P53_S1	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the statement of financial condition.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P53_S2	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P53_S3	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in income currently.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P54_S0	Cash and cash equivalents includes cash and other highly liquid investments with financial institutions containing original maturity dates of 90 days or less.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P54_S1	A portion of the cash designated as Equity in Newedge USA, LLC is restricted and held as margin collateral for futures transactions.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P55_S0	The Partnership maintains a custody account with a major financial institution.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P55_S1	At times, the Partnership s cash balance could exceed the insured amount under the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation ( FDIC ).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P55_S2	The FDIC temporarily increased its limit to $250,000 until December 31, 2013.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P55_S3	The Partnership has not experienced any losses in such accounts and believes it is not subject to any significant credit risk related to its cash account.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P56_S0	The General Partner has incurred all expenses in connection with the initial organization of the Partnership, totaling approximately $64,000.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P56_S1	The General Partner bills the Partnership in monthly installments for such expenses over a sixty month period beginning in the thirteenth month after the Partnership commenced operations.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P56_S2	If the Partnership were to cease operations prior to the end of the sixty month period, the Partnership would not be obligated to pay the General Partner for the unbilled costs.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P57_S0	Offering costs incurred in connection with the ongoing offering of the Partnership s interests are borne by the Partnership.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P57_S2	These costs are charged to partners capital as incurred.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P58_S0	As an entity taxable as a partnership, the Partnership is not itself subject to federal income tax.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P58_S1	The Partnership prepares and files calendar year U.S. and applicable state information tax returns and reports to the partners their allocable shares of the Partnership s income and expenses.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P59_S0	The Partnership is required to determine whether its tax positions are more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority, including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes, based on the technical merits of the position.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P59_S1	The tax benefit recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that has a greater than fifty percent likelihood of being realized upon ultimate settlement with the relevant taxing authority.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P59_S2	De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized results in the Partnership recording a tax liability that reduces ending partners capital.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P59_S3	Based on its analysis, the Partnership has determined that it has not incurred any liability for unrecognized tax benefits as of December 31, 2011 and 2010.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P59_S4	However, the Partnership s conclusions may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including, but not limited to, on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws, regulations and interpretations thereof.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P60_S0	The Partnership recognizes interest and penalties related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and other expenses, respectively.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P60_S1	No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31, 2011, and December 31, 2010 or as of December 31, 2009 and for the period from October 7, 2009 (inception of trading) to December 31, 2009.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P61_S0	The Partnership is subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for all tax years since its inception.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P62_S0	Certain amounts in the 2010 and 2009 financial statements were reclassified to conform to the 2011 presentation.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P63_S0	Investments in the Partnership are made by subscription agreement, subject to acceptance by the General Partner.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P64_S0	The Partnership is not required to make distributions, but may do so at the sole discretion of the General Partner.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P64_S2	The General Partner may request and receive redemption of capital, subject to the same terms as any Limited Partner.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P65_S0	No Limited Partner shall be liable for any debts or liabilities of the Partnership or any losses thereof in excess of such Limited Partner's capital contributions, except as may be required by law.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P66_S0	The Partnership accounts for subscriptions, allocations and redemptions on a per partner capital account basis.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P67_S0	The Partnership consists of the General Partner s Interest, Special Interests, Class A Interests, Class B Interests and Institutional Interests (collectively referred to as Interests ).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P67_S1	Income or loss (prior to management fees, administrative fees, service fees and incentive fees) is allocated pro rata among the partners based on their respective capital accounts as of the end of each month in which the items accrue pursuant to the terms of the Partnership s agreement of limited partnership, as may be amended and restated from time to time (the Agreement ).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P67_S2	Special Interests, Class A Interests, Class B Interests and Institutional Interests are then charged with their applicable management fee, administrative fee, service fee and incentive fee in accordance with the Agreement.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P67_S3	Class A Interests, Class B Interests and Institutional Interests were first issued by the Partnership on October 1, 2009.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P67_S4	The partners may withdraw their interests on a monthly basis upon at least 15 days prior written notice, subject to the discretion of the General Partner.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P68_S0	The General Partner receives from the Partnership a monthly management fee equal to 0.104% (1.25% annually) for Class A and Class B, 0.0625% (0.75% annually) for Institutional Interests, and 0.0208% (0.25% annually) for Special Interests of the Partnership's management fee net asset value (as defined in the Agreement).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P68_S1	The General Partner may declare any limited partner of the Partnership (each, a Limited Partner and collectively the Limited Partners ) a Special Limited Partner and the management fees or incentive fees charged to any such partner may be different than those charged to other Limited Partners.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P76_S0	The Partnership pays to its clearing brokers and Altegris Futures, at a minimum, brokerage charges at a monthly flat rate of 0.125% (1.5% annually) of the Partnership s management fee net asset value (as defined).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P76_S1	Brokerage charges may exceed the flat rate described above, depending on commission and trading volume levels, which may vary.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P77_S1	The Partnership pays the Advisor a quarterly incentive fee of 30% of the trading profits (as defined in the Agreement).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P77_S2	However, the quarterly incentive fee is payable only on cumulative profits, calculated separately for each partner s interest, achieved from commodity trading (as defined in the Agreement).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P77_S3	The incentive fee is accrued on a monthly basis.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P77_S4	Incentive fees are reflected in the statements of operations.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P79_S0	Institutional Interests may pay selling agents, if the selling agent so elects, an ongoing payment of 0.0417% (0.50% annually) of the value of Institutional Interests sold by them which are outstanding at month end as compensation for their continuing services to such Limited Partners holding Institutional Interests.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P81_S1	None of the Partnership s derivative instruments are designated as hedging instruments, as defined in the Derivatives and Hedging Topic of the Accounting Standards Codification, nor are they used for other risk management purposes.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P82_S0	The Advisor and General Partner actively assess, manage and monitor risk exposure on derivatives on a contract basis, a sector basis (e.g., interest rate derivatives, agricultural derivatives, etc.), and on an overall basis in accordance with established risk parameters.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P82_S1	Due to the speculative nature of the Partnership s derivative trading activity, the Partnership is subject to the risk of substantial losses from derivatives trading.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P84_S0	The following presents the trading results of the Partnership s derivative trading and information related to the volume of the Partnership s derivative activity for the years ended December 31, 2011 and 2010 and the period ended October 7, 2009 (inception of trading) to December 31, 2009.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P85_S0	The below captions of Realized and Change in Unrealized correspond to the captions in the statement of operations.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P86_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P86_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P86_S2	Further, the Clearing Broker has the right to require margin in excess of the minimum exchange requirement.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P86_S3	Risk arises from changes in the value of these contracts (market risk) and the potential inability of brokers to perform under the terms of their contracts (credit risk).
1469317_12_ITEM15_P87_S0	All of the contracts currently traded by the Partnership are exchange traded.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P87_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its respective individual counterparties.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P87_S2	However if, in the future, the Partnership were to enter into non-exchange traded contracts, it would be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P87_S3	The credit risk from counterparty non-performance associated with such instruments is the net unrealized gain, if any.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P88_S0	The Partnership also has credit risk because the sole counterparty to all domestic futures contracts is the exchange clearing corporation.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P88_S1	In addition, the Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by the Clearing Broker.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P89_S0	The Partnership's policy is to continuously monitor its exposure to market and counterparty risk through the use of a variety of financial, position and credit exposure reporting and control procedures.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P89_S1	In addition, the Partnership has a policy of reviewing the credit standing of each clearing broker or counterparty with which it conducts business.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P90_S0	Effective as of June 10, 2011 JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A. ( Custodian ) replaced Wilmington Trust Company as the Partnership s custodian.

1469317_12_ITEM15_P93_S0	In May 2011, the FASB issued Accounting Standards Update ( ASU ) No. 2011-04 Amendments to Achieve Common Fair Value Measurement and Disclosure Requirements in U.S. GAAP and International Financial Reporting Standards ( IFRS ) .
1469317_12_ITEM15_P93_S1	ASU 2011-04 includes common requirements for measurement of and disclosure about fair value between U.S. GAAP and IFRS.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P93_S2	ASU 2011-04 will require reporting entities to disclose the following information for fair value measurements categorized within Level 3 of the fair value hierarchy: quantitative information about the unobservable inputs used in the fair value measurement, the valuation processes used by the reporting entity, and a narrative description of the sensitivity of the fair value measurement to changes in unobservable inputs and the interrelationships between those unobservable inputs.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P93_S3	In addition, ASU 2011-04 will require reporting entities to make disclosures about amounts and reasons for all transfers in and out of Level 1 and Level 2 fair value measurements.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P93_S4	The new and revised disclosures are effective for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2011.
1469317_12_ITEM15_P93_S5	At this time, management is evaluating the implications of ASU 2011-04 and its impact on the financial statements.

1469317_13_ITEM1_P0_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. (the Partnership ) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009 and commenced operations following an initial closing on October 1, 2009.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P0_S1	The Partnership is a commodity pool engaged in speculative trading across a broad range of futures contracts and currencies.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P0_S2	The Partnership may in the future trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts (together with futures contracts and currencies, Commodity Interests ).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P1_S0	Under the Partnership s Agreement of Limited Partnership (the Limited Partnership Agreement ), Altegris Portfolio Management, Inc. (d/b/a Altegris Funds), an Arkansas corporation ( Altegris Funds or the General Partner ), serves as general partner of the Partnership and has sole responsibility for management and administration of all aspects of the Partnership s business.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P1_S1	Investors purchasing limited partnership interests (the Interests ) in the Partnership ( Limited Partners and together with the General Partner, Partners ) have no rights to participate in the management of the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P2_S0	Altegris Funds is registered with the Commodity Futures Trading Commission ( CFTC ) as a Commodity Pool Operator ( CPO ), and is a member of National Futures Association ( NFA ).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P2_S1	Quantitative Investment Management LLC, a Virginia limited liability company formed in May 2003, acts as the Partnership s trading advisor ( QIM or the Advisor ).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P2_S2	QIM became registered as a Commodity Trading Advisor ( CTA ) in 2004 and a CPO in 2005 and is a member of NFA.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P2_S3	Effective as of December 31, 2010, Altegris Funds became a wholly-owned subsidiary of Genworth Financial, Inc. ( Genworth ).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P2_S4	Genworth became a principal of Altegris Funds and Altegris Futures, L.L.C. ( Altegris Futures ), an affiliate of the General Partner, in January 2011.

( Altegris Holdings ), a newly-formed indirect holding company subsidiary of Genworth, and contributed all of the outstanding capital stock of Altegris Holdings, Inc. to AssetMark Holdings, Inc. ( AssetMark ), a newly-formed direct subsidiary of Genworth.

1469317_13_ITEM1_P7_S0	The Partnership offers three classes of Interests: Class A, Class B and Institutional Interests (each, a Class of Interest ).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P7_S1	The Classes of Interests differ from each other only in the fees that they pay and the applicable investment minimums.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P8_S0	The Partnership s business constitutes only one segment for financial reporting purposes i.e. , a speculative commodity pool.

1469317_13_ITEM1_P8_S2	Financial information regarding the Partnership s business is set forth in the Partnership s financial statements, included herewith.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P9_S0	The Partnership s objective is to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P10_S0	QIM believes that financial markets are not entirely efficient and that numerous small inefficiencies exist and can be exploited through the prudent use of robust analysis and predictive technologies.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P11_S0	QIM currently employs several thousand quantitative trading models that utilize pattern recognition to predict short-term price movements in global futures markets.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P11_S1	All models are tested across large data sets that expose them to a wide range of market, economic, and political environments, as well as a wide range of time frames and interactions.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P11_S2	Only those models that prove to be the most robust, statistically significant, and conceptually diverse are used in actual trading.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P11_S3	The resultant system of models offers what QIM believes to be reliable signals that guide market timing and trade allocation.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P12_S0	QIM s trading strategies and models may be revised from time to time as a result of ongoing research and development seeking to devise new strategies and systems as well as to improve current methods.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P12_S1	The strategies and systems used by QIM in the future may differ significantly from those currently in use due to changes resulting from this research, and Limited Partners will not be informed of these changes as they may occur.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P13_S0	QIM applies risk management procedures that take into account the price, size, volatility, liquidity, and inter-relationships of the contracts traded.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P13_S1	The Partnership s positions are generally balanced in a manner that allocates approximately equal amounts of measured risk to as many distinct markets as possible and during significant drawdowns in equity, QIM will reduce market exposure by scaling back the Partnership s overall leverage.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P14_S0	QIM s trading is generally approximately 95% systematic and 5% discretionary.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P14_S1	All facets of the predictive models, risk management, and trade allocation are fully automated or proceduralized.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P14_S2	In this sense, the trading is systematic.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P14_S3	Discretion of QIM, however, plays a significant role in the pursuit of improvements to the Program.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P15_S0	QIM has different time horizons for the execution of certain trades.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P15_S1	For example, QIM may have certain trades executed at the beginning of the trading day while giving the executing broker limited discretion with respect to other trades.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P16_S0	QIM currently trades or monitors over 50 tradable markets in currencies, stock indices, interest rates, energy, grains, softs and metals.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P16_S1	QIM may add or delete markets from this universe of tradable markets in its discretion if QIM s research demonstrates that such an addition or deletion would enhance the program s performance.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P17_S0	All markets are futures markets or interbank currency markets.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P18_S0	QIM seeks to profitably trade each of these markets while taking advantage of the diversification available from such a varied universe of futures contracts.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P18_S1	QIM s trading program often takes opposing long and short positions within the same or related classes of correlated futures, which, taken in conjunction with the effect of diversification across a broad range of contracts, generally results in reduced market exposure than trading a single market with similar leverage.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P19_S0	A substantial portion of the equity in the Partnership s account is invested in United States ( U.S. ) government and agency securities and other liquid, high-quality instruments at the direction of the Custodian (as defined below).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P19_S1	QIM will generally maintain an average margin to equity level of between 0% and 20%.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P19_S2	The actual percentage of assets committed to margin at any time may be higher or lower than the target level.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P20_S0	and available for trading by QIM in Commodity Interests on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P20_S1	Interest on Partnership assets held at J.P. Morgan Securities in cash or Treasury securities will be credited to the Partnership as described under Charges.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P20_S2	Depending on market factors, the amount of margin or option premiums held at J.P. Morgan Securities could change significantly, and all of the Partnership s assets are available for use as margin.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P20_S3	The Partnership may also retain other brokers and/or dealers from time to time to clear or execute a portion of Partnership trades made by QIM.

(the Custodian ), the portion not held in checking, money market or other bank accounts (and used to pay Partnership operating expenses) will be invested in liquid, high-quality short-term securities at the direction of the Custodian or its affiliate J.P. Morgan Investment Management Inc. ( JPMIM ).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P21_S1	The Partnership s custody and investment management agreement with the Custodian permits the Custodian to invest in U.S. government and agency securities, other securities or instruments guaranteed by the U.S. government or its agencies, CDs, time deposits, banker s acceptances and commercial paper subject in each case to specific diversification, credit quality and maturity limitations.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P21_S2	The Custodian may use sub-advisers to attempt to increase yield enhancement.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P21_S3	The General Partner may direct that a portion of Partnership assets be deposited with other custodians and retain other sub-advisers for the purpose of attempting to increase yield enhancement via other cash management arrangements.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P22_S0	The percentage of the Partnership s assets deposited with these firms is also subject to change in the General Partner s sole discretion.

1469317_13_ITEM1_P23_S0	The Partnership pays all of its ongoing liabilities, expenses and costs.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P23_S1	Altegris Funds receives a management fee of 0.104% of the prior month ending net asset value, before deduction for any accrued incentive fees related to the current quarter (the management fee net asset value ), of all Class A Interests (1.25% per annum), 0.104% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Class B Interests (1.25% per annum) and 0.0625% of the prior month-end management fee net asset value of all Institutional Interests (0.75% per annum).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P23_S2	QIM receives a 30% of quarterly trading profits applicable to each Class of Interest.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P24_S0	Each selling agent selling Class A Interests receives 0.166% of the month-end net asset value of the Partnership apportioned to each Class A Interest sold by such selling agent (2% per annum) and may elect to receive 0.0417% of the month-end net asset value apportioned to any Institutional Interest sold by such selling (0.50% per annum).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P25_S0	The Partnership s clearing broker paid during 2012 and will pay from and after January 1, 2013 to Altegris Futures a portion of the brokerage commissions and transaction fees received from the Partnership as well as a portion of the interest income received on the Partnership s assets.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P26_S0	Monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_13_ITEM1_P26_S1	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P26_S2	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership pays only the amount described in (A) above.

1469317_13_ITEM1_P30_S0	The CFTC has delegated to NFA responsibility for the registration of commodity trading advisors, commodity pool operators, futures commission merchants, introducing brokers, swap dealers , major swap participants and, in most cases, their respective associated persons, as well as floor brokers and floor traders.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P31_S0	The Commodity Exchange Act requires commodity pool operators such as Altegris Funds, commodity trading advisors such as the Advisor and commodity brokers or FCMs such as J.P. Morgan Securities and introducing brokers such as Altegris Futures to be registered and to comply with various reporting and record keeping requirements.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P31_S1	CFTC regulations also require FCMs and certain introducing brokers to maintain a minimum level of net capital.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P31_S2	In addition, the CFTC and certain commodities exchanges have established limits referred to as speculative position limits on the maximum net long or net short speculative positions that any person may hold or control in any particular futures or options contracts traded on U.S. commodities exchanges.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P31_S3	Similar position limits may in the future be put in place with respect to swaps that are exchange-traded or are economically equivalent to exchange-traded swaps or futures contracts.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P32_S0	All accounts owned or managed by the Advisor will be combined for position limit purposes.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P32_S1	The Advisor could be required to liquidate positions held for the Partnership in order to comply with such limits.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P32_S2	Any such liquidation could result in substantial costs to the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P32_S3	In addition, many futures exchanges impose limits beyond which the price of a futures contract may not trade during the course of a trading day, and there is a potential for a futures contract to hit its daily price limit for several days in a row, making it impossible for the Advisor to liquidate a position and thereby experiencing a dramatic loss.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P33_S0	Certain deliverable currency forward contracts are subject to limited regulation in the United States, including reporting and recordkeeping requirements.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P34_S0	In addition to the registration requirements described above, the CFTC and certain commodity exchanges have established limits on the maximum net long or net short position which any person may hold or control in particular commodities.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P34_S1	Most exchanges also limit the changes in futures contract prices that may occur during a single trading day.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P34_S2	The CFTC may in the future also implement position limits for certain exempt commodity contracts, including metals and energy contracts, with respect to futures, options on futures, and economically equivalent swaps.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P34_S3	Position limits in spot months are proposed to be 25% of the official estimated deliverable supply of the underlying commodity and in a non-spot month a percentage of the average aggregate 12-month rolling open interest in all months (swaps and futures) for each contract.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P34_S4	If such position limits are adopted, they could materially affect the Partnership s trading strategy.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P35_S0	Deliverable currency forward contracts are currently subject to only limited regulation in the United States.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P36_S0	The Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act (the Reform Act ) was enacted in July 2010.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P36_S1	The Reform Act includes provisions that comprehensively regulate the over-the-counter derivatives markets for the first time.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P37_S0	The Reform Act mandates that a substantial portion of over-the-counter derivatives must be executed in regulated markets and submitted for clearing to regulated clearinghouses.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P37_S1	The mandates imposed by the Reform Act may result in the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees with respect to any swaps entered into by the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P38_S0	The Partnership has no operations in foreign countries although it trades on foreign exchanges and other non-U.S. markets.
1469317_13_ITEM1_P38_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.

1469317_13_ITEM7_P1_S0	The Partnership s assets are generally held as cash or cash equivalents, which are used to margin the Partnership s futures positions and are sold to pay redemptions and expenses as needed.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P1_S1	Other than any potential market-imposed limitations on liquidity, the Partnership s assets are highly liquid and are expected to remain so.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P1_S2	Market-imposed limitations, when they occur, can be due to limited open interest in certain futures markets or to daily price fluctuation limits, which are inherent in the Partnership s futures trading.

1469317_13_ITEM7_P3_S0	The Partnership raises additional capital only through the sale of Interests and capital is increased through trading profits (if any) and interest income.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P3_S1	The Partnership does not engage in borrowing.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P4_S0	The amount of capital raised for the Partnership should not have a significant impact on its operations, as the Partnership has no significant capital expenditure or working capital requirements other than for capital to pay trading losses, brokerage commissions and expenses.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P4_S1	Within broad ranges of capitalization, the Partnership s trading positions should increase or decrease in approximate proportion to the size of the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P5_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts and may trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P5_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P5_S2	Further, the Partnership s FCMs and brokers may require margin in excess of minimum exchange requirements.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P6_S0	All of the futures contracts currently traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership are exchange-traded.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P6_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its trading counterparties, whereas exchange-traded contracts are generally, but not universally, backed by the collective credit of the members of the exchange.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P6_S2	In the future, the Partnership anticipates that it will enter into non-exchange-traded foreign currency contracts and be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P7_S0	The Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by J.P. Morgan Securities and/or other clearing brokers or counterparties with which the Partnership trades.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P8_S0	The Partnership s success depends primarily upon QIM s ability to recognize and capitalize on market trends in the sectors of the global commodity futures markets in which it trades.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P8_S1	The Partnership seeks to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P8_S2	The past performance of the Partnership is not necessarily indicative of future results.

1469317_13_ITEM7_P37_S0	The Partnership does not engage in off-balance sheet arrangements with other entities.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P38_S0	Altegris Funds believes that the Partnership s most critical accounting estimates relate to the valuation of the Partnership s assets.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P39_S0	Futures and options on futures contracts are valued using the primary exchange s closing price.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P39_S1	Forward currency contracts are stated at fair value using spot currency rates provided by J.P. Morgan Securities and adjusted for interest rates and other typical adjustment factors.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P40_S0	U.S. government agency securities are generally valued based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P40_S1	Corporate notes and repurchase agreements are generally valued at fair value.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P40_S2	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P40_S3	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P41_S0	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the statement of financial condition.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P41_S1	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P41_S2	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in income currently.

1469317_13_ITEM7_P42_S1	Actual results could differ from those estimates.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P42_S2	Based on the nature of the business and operations of the Partnership, Altegris Funds believes that the estimates utilized in preparing the Partnership s financial statements are appropriate and reasonable, however, actual results could differ from these estimates.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P42_S3	The estimates used do not provide a range of possible results that would require the exercise of subjective judgment.
1469317_13_ITEM7_P42_S4	Altegris Funds further believes that, based on the nature of the business and operations of the Partnership, no other reasonable assumptions relating to the application of the Partnership s critical accounting estimates other than those currently used would likely result in materially different amounts from those reported.

1469317_13_ITEM9A_P0_S0	(a) The General Partner, with the participation of the General Partner s principal executive officer and principal financial officer, has evaluated the effectiveness of the design and operation of its disclosure controls and procedures with respect to the Partnership as of the end of the period covered by this annual report, and, based on their evaluation, has concluded that these disclosure controls and procedures are effective.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P1_S0	Altegris Funds, the general partner of the Partnership is responsible for the management of the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management of Altegris Funds ( Management ) is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P2_S1	The internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P3_S0	Provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or disposition of the Partnership s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P4_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P4_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P5_S0	Management assessed the effectiveness of the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting as of December 31, 2012.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P5_S1	In making this assessment, Management used the criteria set forth in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission ( COSO ).
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P5_S2	As a result of this assessment and based on the criteria in the COSO framework, management has concluded that, as of December 31, 2012, the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting was effective.
1469317_13_ITEM9A_P6_S0	There were no changes in the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting during the quarter ended December 31, 2012 that have materially affected, or are reasonably likely to materially affect, its internal control over financial reporting.

1469317_13_ITEM11_P2_S0	From January 1, 2012, Altegris Futures, in its capacity as Introducing Broker to the Partnership, received compensation for brokerage-related services.
1469317_13_ITEM11_P2_S1	The Partnership will pay monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_13_ITEM11_P2_S2	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_13_ITEM11_P2_S3	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay only the amount described in (A) above.

1469317_13_ITEM15_P15_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. ( Partnership ) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P15_S1	The Partnership's general partner is Altegris Portfolio Management, Inc. (d/b/a Altegris Funds) ("General Partner").
1469317_13_ITEM15_P16_S0	The Partnership speculatively trades commodity futures contracts, and may trade options on futures contracts, forward contracts and other commodity interests.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P17_S0	The objective of the Partnership s business is appreciation of its assets.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P17_S1	It is subject to the regulations of the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (the CFTC ), an agency of the United States ( U.S. ) government that regulates most aspects of the commodity futures industry; rules of the National Futures Association, an industry self-regulatory organization; and the requirements of commodity exchanges and Futures Commission Merchants (brokers) through which the Partnership trades.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P18_S0	The Partnership s financial statements are presented in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles ( U.S. GAAP ).
1469317_13_ITEM15_P18_S1	The preparation of the financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported fair value of assets and liabilities, disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities as of December 31, 2012 and 2011, and reported amounts of income and expenses for the years ended December 31, 2012, 2011 and 2010, respectively.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P18_S2	Management believes that the estimates utilized in preparing the Partnership s financial statements are reasonable; however, actual results could differ from these estimates and it is reasonably possible that the differences could be material.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P19_S0	In accordance with the authoritative guidance under U.S. GAAP, fair value is defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability (i.e. the exit price ) in an orderly transaction between market participants at the measurement date.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P20_S0	In determining fair value, the Partnership uses various valuation approaches.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P21_S0	The authoritative guidance under U.S. GAAP establishes a fair value hierarchy for inputs used in measuring fair value that maximizes the use of observable inputs and minimizes the use of unobservable inputs by requiring that the most observable inputs be used when available.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P22_S0	Observable inputs are those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability based on market data obtained from sources independent of the Partnership.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P23_S0	Unobservable inputs reflect the Partnership s assumption about the inputs market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability developed based on the best information available in the circumstances.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P23_S1	The fair value hierarchy is categorized into three levels based on the inputs as follows:
1469317_13_ITEM15_P24_S0	Level 1 - Valuations based on unadjusted quoted prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities that the Partnership has the ability to access.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P25_S0	Level 2 - Valuations based on quoted prices in markets that are not active or for which all significant inputs are observable, either directly or indirectly.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P26_S0	Level 3 - Valuations based on inputs that are unobservable.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P27_S0	The availability of valuation techniques and observable inputs can vary among assets and liabilities and is affected by a wide variety of factors, including the type of asset or liability, whether the asset or liability is new and not yet established in the marketplace, and other characteristics particular to the transaction.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P28_S0	To the extent that valuation is based on models or inputs that are less observable or unobservable in the market, the determination of fair value requires more judgment.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P28_S1	Those estimated values do not necessarily represent the amounts that may be ultimately realized due to the occurrence of future circumstances that cannot be reasonably determined.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P28_S2	Because of the inherent uncertainty of valuation, those estimated values may be materially higher or lower than the values that would have been used had a ready market for the asset or liability existed.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P28_S3	Accordingly, the degree of judgment exercised by the Partnership in determining fair value is greatest for assets and liabilities categorized in Level 3.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P29_S0	In certain cases, the inputs used to measure fair value may fall into different levels of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P29_S1	In such cases, for disclosure purposes, the level in the fair value hierarchy within which the fair value measurement falls in its entirety is determined by the lowest level input that is significant to the fair value measurement.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P30_S0	Fair value is a market-based measure considered from the perspective of a market participant rather than an entity-specific measure.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P30_S1	Therefore, even when market assumptions are not readily available, the Partnership s own assumptions are set to reflect those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability at the measurement date.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P31_S0	The Partnership uses prices and inputs that are current as of the measurement date, including prices and inputs during periods of market dislocation.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P31_S1	In periods of market dislocation, the observability of prices and inputs may be reduced for many assets and liabilities.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P31_S2	This condition could cause an asset or liability to be reclassified to a lower level within the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P32_S0	The Partnership values futures contracts at the closing price of the contract s primary exchange.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P32_S1	The Partnership includes futures contracts in Level 1 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P33_S0	The fair value of U.S. government agency bonds and notes is generally based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P33_S1	When quoted prices are not available, fair value is determined based on a valuation model that uses inputs which include interest-rate yield curves, cross-currency-basis index spreads, and country credit spreads similar to the bond in terms of issue, maturity and seniority.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P34_S0	U.S. government agency bonds and notes are generally categorized in Levels 1 or 2 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P34_S1	No U.S. government agency bonds and notes were fair valued using valuation models as of December 31, 2012 and 2011.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P35_S0	The fair value of U.S. treasury obligations is generally based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P35_S1	U.S. treasury obligations are generally categorized in Level 1 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P36_S0	The fair value of corporate notes is determined using recently executed transactions, market price quotations (where observable), notes spreads or credit default swap spreads.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P36_S1	The spread data used are for the same maturity as that of the notes.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P36_S2	If the spread data does not reference the issuer, data that references a comparable issuer is used.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P37_S0	When observable price quotations are not available, fair value is determined based on cash flow models with yield curves, notes, or single-name credit default swap spreads and recovery rates based on collateral values as key inputs.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P37_S1	These valuation methods represent both a market and income approach to fair value measurement.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P38_S0	Corporate notes are generally categorized in Level 2 of the fair value hierarchy; however, in instances where significant inputs are unobservable, they are categorized in Level 3 of the hierarchy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P38_S1	No corporate notes were fair valued using valuation models as of December 31, 2012 and 2011.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P39_S0	The inputs or methodology used for valuing securities are not necessarily an indication of the risk associated with investing in those securities.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P39_S1	There were no changes in the Partnership s valuation methodology during the years ended December 31, 2012 and 2011.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P40_S0	The following table presents information about the Partnership s assets and liabilities measured at fair value as of December 31, 2012 and December 31, 2011:
1469317_13_ITEM15_P41_S0	"Financial Derivative Instruments" for the fair value in each type of contracts within this category.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P42_S0	For the years ended December 31, 2012 and 2011, there were no transfers between Level 1 and Level 2 assets and liabilities.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P42_S1	For the years ended December 31, 2012 and 2011, there were no Level 3 securities.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P43_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date for financial reporting purposes.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P43_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P43_S2	Change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the Statements of Operations.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P44_S0	Brokerage commissions and other trading fees are reflected as an adjustment to cost or proceeds at the time of the transaction.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P45_S0	Interest income is recorded on an accrual basis.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P46_S0	Gains or losses on futures contracts are realized when contracts are closed.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P46_S1	Net unrealized gains or losses on open contracts (the difference between contract trade price and quoted market price) are reflected in the Statements of Financial Condition.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P46_S2	Any change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the Statements of Operations.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P47_S0	Brokerage commissions on futures contracts include other trading fees and are incurred as an expense when contracts are opened.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P48_S0	The Partnership may invest in futures contracts as part of its investment strategy.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P49_S0	Upon entering into a futures contract, the Partnership is required to deposit with the broker an amount of cash or cash equivalents equal to a certain percentage of the contract amount.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P49_S1	This is known as the initial margin.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P49_S2	Subsequent payments ( variation margin ) are made or received by the Partnership each day, depending on the daily fluctuations in the value of the contract, and are included in unrealized gain (loss) on futures contracts.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P50_S0	The Partnership recognizes a realized gain or loss when the contract is closed.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P51_S0	There are several risks in connection with the use of futures contracts as an investment option.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P52_S0	The change in value of futures contracts primarily corresponds with the value of their underlying instruments.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P52_S1	In addition, there is the risk that the Partnership may not be able to enter into a closing transaction because of an illiquid secondary market.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P52_S2	Open positions in futures contracts at December 31, 2012 and 2011 are reflected within the Condensed Schedules of Investments.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P53_S0	The Partnership s functional currency is the U.S. dollar; however, it transacts business in currencies other than the U.S. dollar.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P53_S1	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the Statements of Financial Condition.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P53_S2	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P53_S3	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in the Statement of Operations.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P54_S0	Restricted cash is held as margin collateral for futures transactions.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P55_S0	The Partnership maintains a custody account with a major financial institution.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P55_S1	At times, the Partnership s cash balance could exceed the insured amount under the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation ( FDIC ).
1469317_13_ITEM15_P55_S2	The FDIC temporarily increased its limit to $250,000 until December 31, 2013.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P55_S3	The Partnership has not experienced any losses in such accounts and believes it is not subject to any significant counterparty risk related to its cash account.

1469317_13_ITEM15_P56_S2	These costs are charged as an expense when incurred.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P57_S0	As an entity taxable as a partnership for U.S. Federal income tax purposes; the Partnership itself is not subject to federal income tax.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P57_S1	The Partnership prepares and files calendar year U.S. and applicable state information tax returns and reports to the partners their allocable shares of the Partnership s income and expenses.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P58_S0	The Partnership is required to determine whether its tax positions are more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority, including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes, based on the technical merits of the position.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P58_S1	The tax benefit recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that has a greater than fifty percent likelihood of being realized upon ultimate settlement with the relevant taxing authority.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P58_S2	De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized results in the Partnership recording a tax liability that reduces ending partners capital.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P58_S3	Based on its analysis, the Partnership has determined that it has not incurred any liability for unrecognized tax benefits as of December 31, 2012 and 2011.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P58_S4	However, the Partnership s conclusions may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including, but not limited to, on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws, regulations and interpretations thereof.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P59_S0	The Partnership recognizes interest and penalties related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and other expenses, respectively.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P59_S1	No interest expense or penalties have been recognized for the years ended December 31, 2012, 2011 and 2010.

1469317_13_ITEM15_P86_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P86_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P86_S2	Further, the Clearing Broker has the right to require margin in excess of the minimum exchange requirement.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P86_S3	Risk arises from changes in the value of these contracts (market risk) and the potential inability of brokers to perform under the terms of their contracts (credit risk).
1469317_13_ITEM15_P87_S0	All of the contracts currently traded by the Partnership are exchange traded.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P87_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its respective individual counterparties.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P87_S2	However, in the future, if the Partnership were to enter into non-exchange traded contracts, it would be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P87_S3	The credit risk from counterparty non-performance associated with such instruments is the net unrealized gain, if any.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P88_S0	The Partnership also has credit risk because the sole counterparty to all domestic futures contracts is the exchange clearing corporation.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P88_S1	In addition, the Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by the Clearing Broker.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P89_S0	The Partnership's policy is to continuously monitor its exposure to market and counterparty risk through the use of a variety of financial, position and credit exposure reporting and control procedures.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P89_S1	In addition, the Partnership has a policy of reviewing the credit standing of each clearing broker or counterparty with which it conducts business.

1469317_13_ITEM15_P90_S3	The Partnership has a substantial portion of its assets on deposit with the Custodian in U.S. government agency bonds and notes and corporate notes.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P91_S0	Risks arise from investments in bonds and notes due to possible illiquidity and the potential for default by the issuer or counterparty.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P91_S1	Such instruments are also sensitive to changes in interest rates and economic conditions.

1469317_13_ITEM15_P92_S1	The Partnership s maximum exposure under these arrangements is unknown, as this would involve future claims that may be made against the Partnership that have not yet occurred.
1469317_13_ITEM15_P92_S2	The Partnership expects the risk of any future obligation under these indemnifications to be remote.

1469317_14_ITEM1_P0_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. (the Partnership ) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009 and commenced operations following an initial closing on October 1, 2009.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P0_S1	The Partnership is a commodity pool engaged in speculative trading across a broad range of futures contracts and currencies.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P0_S2	The Partnership may in the future trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts (together with futures contracts and currencies, Commodity Interests ).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P1_S0	Under the Partnership s Agreement of Limited Partnership (the Limited Partnership Agreement ), Altegris Portfolio Management, Inc. (d/b/a Altegris Funds), an Arkansas corporation ( Altegris Funds or the General Partner ), serves as general partner of the Partnership and has sole responsibility for management and administration of all aspects of the Partnership s business.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P1_S1	Investors purchasing limited partnership interests (the Interests ) in the Partnership ( Limited Partners and together with the General Partner, Partners ) have no rights to participate in the management of the Partnership.
