1469317_14_ITEM1_P9_S1	The Classes of Interests differ from each other only in the fees that they pay and the applicable investment minimums.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P10_S0	The Partnership s business constitutes only one segment for financial reporting purposes i.e. , a speculative commodity pool.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P10_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P10_S2	Financial information regarding the Partnership s business is set forth in the Partnership s financial statements, included herewith.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P11_S0	The Partnership s objective is to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P12_S0	QIM believes that financial markets are not entirely efficient and that numerous small inefficiencies exist and can be exploited through the prudent use of robust analysis and predictive technologies.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P13_S0	QIM currently employs several thousand quantitative trading models that utilize pattern recognition to predict short-term price movements in global futures markets.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P13_S1	All models are tested across large data sets that expose them to a wide range of market, economic, and political environments, as well as a wide range of time frames and interactions.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P13_S2	Only those models that prove to be the most robust, statistically significant, and conceptually diverse are used in actual trading.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P13_S3	The resultant system of models offers what QIM believes to be reliable signals that guide market timing and trade allocation.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P14_S0	QIM s trading strategies and models may be revised from time to time as a result of ongoing research and development seeking to devise new strategies and systems as well as to improve current methods.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P14_S1	The strategies and systems used by QIM in the future may differ significantly from those currently in use due to changes resulting from this research, and Limited Partners will not be informed of these changes as they may occur.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P15_S0	QIM applies risk management procedures that take into account the price, size, volatility, liquidity, and inter-relationships of the contracts traded.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P15_S1	The Partnership s positions are generally balanced in a manner that allocates approximately equal amounts of measured risk to as many distinct markets as possible and during significant drawdowns in equity, QIM will reduce market exposure by scaling back the Partnership s overall leverage.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P16_S0	QIM s trading is generally approximately 95% systematic and 5% discretionary.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P16_S1	All facets of the predictive models, risk management, and trade allocation are fully automated or proceduralized.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P16_S2	In this sense, the trading is systematic.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P16_S3	Discretion of QIM, however, plays a significant role in the pursuit of improvements to the Program.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P17_S0	QIM has different time horizons for the execution of certain trades.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P17_S1	For example, QIM may have certain trades executed at the beginning of the trading day while giving the executing broker limited discretion with respect to other trades.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P18_S0	QIM currently trades or monitors over 50 tradable markets in currencies, stock indices, interest rates, energy, grains, softs and metals.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P18_S1	QIM may add or delete markets from this universe of tradable markets in its discretion if QIM s research demonstrates that such an addition or deletion would enhance the program s performance.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P19_S0	All markets are futures markets or interbank currency markets.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P20_S0	QIM seeks to profitably trade each of these markets while taking advantage of the diversification available from such a varied universe of futures contracts.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P20_S1	QIM s trading program often takes opposing long and short positions within the same or related classes of correlated futures, which, taken in conjunction with the effect of diversification across a broad range of contracts, generally results in reduced market exposure than trading a single market with similar leverage.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P21_S0	A substantial portion of the equity in the Partnership s account is invested in United States ( U.S. ) government and agency securities and other liquid, high-quality instruments at the direction of the Custodian (as defined below).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P21_S1	QIM will generally maintain an average margin to equity level of between 0% and 20%.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P21_S2	The actual percentage of assets committed to margin at any time may be higher or lower than the target level.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P22_S0	It is expected that between 5% and 20% of the Partnership s assets generally will be held as initial margin or option premiums (in cash or U.S. Treasury Department ( Treasury ) securities) in the Partnership s brokerage accounts at its clearing broker, J.P. Morgan Securities LLC ( J.P. Morgan Securities ), a futures commission merchant ( FCM ), and available for trading by QIM in Commodity Interests on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P22_S1	Interest on Partnership assets held at J.P. Morgan Securities in cash or Treasury securities will be credited to the Partnership as described under Charges.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P22_S2	Depending on market factors, the amount of margin or option premiums held at J.P. Morgan Securities could change significantly, and all of the Partnership s assets are available for use as margin.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P22_S3	The Partnership may also retain other brokers and/or dealers from time to time to clear or execute a portion of Partnership trades made by QIM.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P23_S0	With respect to Partnership assets not held at J.P. Morgan Securities as described above, but deposited with JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A. (the Custodian ), the portion not held in checking, money market or other bank accounts (and used to pay Partnership operating expenses) will be invested in liquid, high-quality short-term securities at the direction of the Custodian or its affiliate J.P. Morgan Investment Management Inc. ( JPMIM ).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P23_S1	The Partnership s custody and investment management agreement with the Custodian permits the Custodian to invest in U.S. government and agency securities, other securities or instruments guaranteed by the U.S. government or its agencies, CDs, time deposits, banker s acceptances and commercial paper subject in each case to specific diversification, credit quality and maturity limitations.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P23_S2	The Custodian may use sub-advisers to attempt to increase yield enhancement.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P23_S3	The General Partner may direct that a portion of Partnership assets be deposited with other custodians and retain other sub-advisers for the purpose of attempting to increase yield enhancement via other cash management arrangements.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P24_S0	The percentage of the Partnership s assets deposited with these firms is also subject to change in the General Partner s sole discretion.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P24_S1	The Partnership s assets will not be commingled with the assets of any other person.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P24_S2	Depositing the Partnership s assets with banks or J.P. Morgan Securities, or other clearing brokers, as segregated funds is not commingling for these purposes.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P25_S0	The Partnership pays all of its ongoing liabilities, expenses and costs.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P26_S0	Altegris Funds receives a management fee of 0.104% of the month-end net asset value, before deduction for any accrued incentive fees related to the current quarter (the management fee net asset value ), of all Class A Interests (1.25% per annum), 0.104% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Class B Interests (1.25% per annum) and 0.0625% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Institutional Interests (0.75% per annum).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P26_S1	QIM receives a 30% of quarterly trading profits applicable to each Class of Interest.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P27_S0	Each selling agent selling Class A Interests receives 0.166% of the month-end net asset value of the Partnership apportioned to each Class A Interest sold by such selling agent (2% per annum) and may elect to receive 0.0417% of the month-end net asset value apportioned to any Institutional Interest sold by such selling (0.50% per annum).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P28_S0	J.P. Morgan Securities paid during 2013 to Altegris Futures a portion of the brokerage commissions and transaction fees received from the Partnership as well as a portion of the interest income received on the Partnership s assets.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P28_S1	Monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P28_S2	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P28_S3	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership pays only the amount described in (A) above.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P29_S0	The Partnership generally pays its operating expenses as they are incurred.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P29_S1	However, during the first twelve months after the Partnership commenced trading, the General Partner agreed to limit the operating expenses paid by the Partnership to 1/12 th of 0.5% of the month-end capital account balances of all Interests for such month.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P30_S0	A fixed administrative fee is charged to Class A and Class B Interests and paid to Altegris Funds equal to 0.0275% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balance of all such Class A and Class B Interests (0.333% per annum).
1469317_14_ITEM1_P31_S0	The CFTC has delegated to NFA responsibility for the registration of commodity trading advisors, commodity pool operators, futures commission merchants, introducing brokers, swap dealers , major swap participants and, in most cases, their respective associated persons, as well as floor brokers and floor traders.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P32_S0	The Commodity Exchange Act requires commodity pool operators such as Altegris Funds, commodity trading advisors such as the Advisor and commodity brokers or FCMs such as J.P. Morgan Securities and introducing brokers such as Altegris Futures to be registered and to comply with various reporting and record keeping requirements.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P32_S1	CFTC regulations also require FCMs and certain introducing brokers to maintain a minimum level of net capital.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P32_S2	In addition, the CFTC and certain commodities exchanges have established limits referred to as speculative position limits on the maximum net long or net short speculative positions that any person may hold or control in any particular futures or options contracts traded on U.S. commodities exchanges.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P32_S3	Similar position limits may in the future be put in place with respect to swaps that are exchange-traded or are economically equivalent to exchange-traded swaps or futures contracts.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P33_S0	All accounts owned or managed by the Advisor will be combined for position limit purposes.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P33_S1	The Advisor could be required to liquidate positions held for the Partnership in order to comply with such limits.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P33_S2	Any such liquidation could result in substantial costs to the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P33_S3	In addition, many futures exchanges impose limits beyond which the price of a futures contract may not trade during the course of a trading day, and there is a potential for a futures contract to hit its daily price limit for several days in a row, making it impossible for the Advisor to liquidate a position and thereby experiencing a dramatic loss.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P34_S0	Certain deliverable currency forward contracts are subject to limited regulation in the U.S., including reporting and recordkeeping requirements.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P35_S0	In addition to the registration requirements described above, the CFTC and certain commodity exchanges have established limits on the maximum net long or net short position which any person may hold or control in particular commodities.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P35_S1	Most exchanges also limit the changes in futures contract prices that may occur during a single trading day.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P35_S2	The CFTC may in the future also implement position limits for certain exempt commodity contracts, including metals and energy contracts, with respect to futures, options on futures, and economically equivalent swaps.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P35_S3	Position limits in spot months are proposed to be 25% of the official estimated deliverable supply of the underlying commodity and in a non-spot month a percentage of the average aggregate 12-month rolling open interest in all months (swaps and futures) for each contract.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P35_S4	If such position limits are adopted, they could materially affect the Partnership s trading strategy.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P36_S0	Deliverable currency forward contracts are currently subject to only limited regulation in the United States.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P37_S0	The Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act (the Reform Act ) was enacted in July 2010.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P37_S1	The Reform Act includes provisions that comprehensively regulate the over-the-counter derivatives markets for the first time.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P38_S0	The Reform Act mandates that a substantial portion of over-the-counter derivatives must be executed in regulated markets and submitted for clearing to regulated clearinghouses.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P38_S1	The mandates imposed by the Reform Act may result in the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees with respect to any swaps entered into by the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P39_S0	The Partnership has no operations in foreign countries although it trades on foreign exchanges and other non-U.S. markets.
1469317_14_ITEM1_P39_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.
1469317_14_ITEM2_P0_S0	The Partnership does not own or use any physical properties in the conduct of its business.
1469317_14_ITEM2_P0_S1	Employees of the General Partner and its affiliates, perform all administrative services for the Partnership from offices located at 1200 Prospect Street, Suite 400, La Jolla, CA 92037.

1469317_14_ITEM3_P0_S1	The Partnership is not aware of any material legal proceedings involving Altegris Funds or its principals in an adverse position to the Partnership or in which the Partnership has adverse interests.

1469317_14_ITEM7_P1_S0	The Partnership s assets are generally held as cash or cash equivalents, which are used to margin the Partnership s futures positions and are sold to pay redemptions and expenses as needed.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P1_S1	Other than any potential market-imposed limitations on liquidity, the Partnership s assets are highly liquid and are expected to remain so.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P1_S2	Market-imposed limitations, when they occur, can be due to limited open interest in certain futures markets or to daily price fluctuation limits, which are inherent in the Partnership s futures trading.

1469317_14_ITEM7_P2_S1	Through December 31, 2013 the Partnership experienced no meaningful periods of illiquidity in any of the markets traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P3_S0	The Partnership raises additional capital only through the sale of Interests and capital is increased through trading profits (if any) and interest income.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P3_S1	The Partnership does not engage in borrowing.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P4_S0	The amount of capital raised for the Partnership should not have a significant impact on its operations, as the Partnership has no significant capital expenditure or working capital requirements other than for capital to pay trading losses, brokerage commissions and expenses.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P4_S1	Within broad ranges of capitalization, the Partnership s trading positions should increase or decrease in approximate proportion to the size of the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P5_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts and may trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P5_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P5_S2	Further, the Partnership s FCMs and brokers may require margin in excess of minimum exchange requirements.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P6_S0	All of the futures contracts currently traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership are exchange-traded.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P6_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its trading counterparties, whereas exchange-traded contracts are generally, but not universally, backed by the collective credit of the members of the exchange.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P6_S2	In the future, the Partnership anticipates that it will enter into non-exchange-traded foreign currency contracts and be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P7_S0	The Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by J.P. Morgan Securities and/or other clearing brokers or counterparties with which the Partnership trades.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P8_S0	The Partnership s success depends primarily upon QIM s ability to recognize and capitalize on market trends in the sectors of the global commodity futures markets in which it trades.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P8_S1	The Partnership seeks to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P8_S2	The past performance of the Partnership is not necessarily indicative of future results.

1469317_14_ITEM7_P24_S7	Subdued data from China, Europe and the US housing market also contributed to the rally in interest rate futures for the remainder of the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P24_S8	While the Partnership lightened its exposure to US interest rates, positions in the European rates lead to losses in those markets.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P24_S9	The Partnership profited from its trading of futures contracts on the short side of the Yen and on the long side of E-mini S P contracts during the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P25_S0	During 2011, the Partnership achieved net realized and unrealized gains of $4,717,099 from all trading: losses of $4,619,789 from trading of derivatives including brokerage commissions paid of $1,941,056.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P25_S1	The Partnership accrued total expenses of $4,578,825, including $969,544 in incentive fees, $1,462,413 in management fees paid to the General Partner, and $1,482,904 in service and professional fees.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P25_S2	The Partnership earned $266,259 in interest income during 2011.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P25_S3	An analysis of the profits and losses generated from the Partnership s commodity futures trading activities for each quarter during 2011 is set forth below.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S0	The Partnership achieved a gain in October 2011 as the program continued to benefit from turbulence in stock index and interest rate futures.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S1	Equity markets rebounded strongly from their five-month free fall; however, markets began to sell off again at month-end.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S2	The Partnership profitably traded Euro-Bund futures contracts and took advantage of rising interest rates on the long end of the US yield curve.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S3	Trading in Euro futures continued to be strong as the currency gained in conjunction with renewed investor confidence.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S4	Crude oil futures also played a positive role in the month s final tally.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S5	The Partnership achieved a gain in November 2011 booking large gains on the first and last day of the month, and was profitable on five of the last six trading days of November.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S6	On the first of the month, when the program was largely short stock index futures and long interest rates, the Greek government called for a referendum on the latest bailout package causing the markets to fall and interest rate futures to rally sharply, producing large gains.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P26_S7	Euro-Bund and Dax futures were the most profitable contracts during the month, as the Partnership took advantage of continued volatility in Europe.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P27_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in October 2011.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P28_S0	Trading in futures contracts on US Treasury notes and bonds proved challenging as news continued to fuel uncertainty regarding the European monetary union.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P28_S1	The Partnership also lost money in futures contracts on the Nasdaq and S P 500.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P28_S2	Euro currency and Euro-Bund trading were among the Partnership s most lucrative contracts.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P28_S3	The program held short positions in gold futures for all but the last day of the month, during which time the price of gold contracts dropped significantly.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P29_S0	Performance in July was positive as trading in interest rate futures showed solid gains.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P29_S1	Performance was boosted by gold and silver trading as the gold markets reached an all-time high.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P29_S2	The end of the month saw global markets falter and the Partnership s short stock index positions and long interest rate positions, generated gains for the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S0	August saw mixed performance for the Partnership as world equity markets, which had fallen significantly in the last week of July, fell even more rapidly in the first week of August.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S1	The Partnership began the month with gains primarily from its positions in US and European stock index futures, but concerns regarding the European debt crisis and the downgrade of US Government debt drove markets significantly lower.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S2	Performance was driven by positions in equity markets - both short and long.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S3	The Partnership achieved gains in trading gold futures amid a choppy market for the commodity.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S4	The partnership achieved a gain in September 2011 as markets continued to be driven by speculation regarding the sovereign debt crises throughout the euro zone.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S5	The Partnership was well-positioned to take advantage of high volatility by holding short positions in global equity markets and long positions in global interest rate futures to start the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P30_S6	The Partnership profited by reversing its positions as the markets rallied during the second week of the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P31_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in April 2011, as news of the severity of the Japanese nuclear crisis hurt long positions the Partnership held in futures contracts on global equities, the U.S. dollar and crude oil.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P31_S1	The Partnership also held short positions in futures contracts in silver, as the price of silver posted its largest monthly gain in nearly 30 years, making silver the worst performing market this month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P31_S2	Gains in trading futures contracts in gold, the Australian dollar and European interest rates were not enough to offset losses elsewhere in the portfolio.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P31_S3	The Partnership experienced a loss in May 2011.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S0	Long positions in futures on the U.S. dollar and short crude positions exploited weaknesses in those markets and led to modest gains.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S1	Despite these early gains, the Partnership closed the month with six consecutive down days on trading in futures contracts on foreign currencies, silver, and U.S. equities.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S2	The Partnership experienced a loss in June 2011.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S3	The Partnership suffered from its long positions in futures contracts on the S P 500 on the worst day of the year for that index.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S4	Losses in currency trading occurred primarily in the euro and Canadian dollar.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S5	Silver trading was the program s best performing market, with the Partnership holding short positions as the price of silver fell during the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P32_S6	The Partnership traded well in futures contracts on U.S. and European bonds boosting returns in interest rates, however performance overall was negative at month end.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in January 2011, as markets reacted strongly to political unrest in Egypt.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S1	The Partnership was well positioned to take advantage of movements in the price of futures contracts on the Euro, which secured some gains.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S2	An extended short position in futures contracts on Silver also added positively to performance.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S3	The Partnership ended the month down on difficult trading of crude oil futures at the end of the month.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S4	The Partnership achieved a gain in February 2011.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S5	Strong trading in stock index futures and U.S. interest rates drove February performance as unrest in the Middle East increased volatility in world markets.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S6	The Partnership participated on both sides of the market as volatility in the medium and long-term U.S. treasury futures helped to generate profits.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S7	Trading on currency futures was flat for the month, despite significant gains in trading futures contracts on the Euro.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S8	The Partnership experienced a loss in March 2011.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S9	The Partnership suffered losses on long positions in Japanese equities and crude oil as news of the earthquake in Japan broke.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S10	The Partnership increased its long positions in futures contracts on Japanese equities as the markets fell, and the subsequent rebound made up for the initial losses.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P33_S11	Gains in trading futures contracts on the Euro were offset by losses in futures contracts on the U.S. Treasury markets, as the Partnership ended the month down.

1469317_14_ITEM7_P35_S0	Altegris Funds believes that the Partnership s most critical accounting estimates relate to the valuation of the Partnership s assets.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P36_S0	Futures and options on futures contracts are valued using the primary exchange s closing price.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P36_S1	Foreign currency contracts are stated at fair value using spot currency rates provided by J.P. Morgan Securities and adjusted for interest rates and other typical adjustment factors.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P37_S0	U.S. government agency securities are generally valued based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P37_S1	Corporate notes and repurchase agreements are generally valued at fair value, which usually approximates cost, given their short duration from the time of purchase.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P38_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P38_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the identified cost method.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P39_S0	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the statement of financial condition.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P39_S1	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_14_ITEM7_P39_S2	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in income currently.

1469317_14_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management of Altegris Funds ( Management ) is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting.
1469317_14_ITEM9A_P2_S1	The internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
1469317_14_ITEM9A_P3_S0	Provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or disposition of the Partnership s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
1469317_14_ITEM9A_P4_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
1469317_14_ITEM9A_P4_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.

1469317_14_ITEM11_P1_S0	Altegris Funds receives a monthly management fee equal to 1/12 of 1.25% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Class A and Class B Interests and equal to 1/12 of 0.75% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Institutional Interests.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P1_S1	Altegris Funds also receives a monthly administrative fee equal to 1/12 of 0.333% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balances attributable to Class A and Class B Interests.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P2_S0	Altegris receives continuing monthly compensation from the Partnership equal to 1/12 of 2% of the month-end net asset value of Class A Interests sold by Altegris.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P3_S0	Altegris Futures, in its capacity as Introducing Broker to the Partnership, received compensation for brokerage-related services.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P3_S1	The Partnership will pay monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_14_ITEM11_P3_S2	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P3_S3	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay only the amount described in (A) above.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P4_S0	The Partnership has no other compensation arrangements.
1469317_14_ITEM11_P4_S1	There are no compensation plans or arrangements relating to a change in control of the Partnership.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P15_S0	Altegris QIM Futures Fund, L.P. ( Partnership ) was organized as a Delaware limited partnership in June 2009.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P15_S1	The Partnership's general partner is Altegris Portfolio Management, Inc. (d/b/a Altegris Funds) ("General Partner").
1469317_14_ITEM15_P16_S0	The Partnership speculatively trades commodity futures contracts, and may trade options on futures contracts, forward contracts and other commodity interests.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P17_S0	The objective of the Partnership s business is appreciation of its assets.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P17_S1	It is subject to the regulations of the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (the CFTC ), an agency of the United States ( U.S. ) government that regulates most aspects of the commodity futures industry; rules of the National Futures Association, an industry self-regulatory organization; and the requirements of commodity exchanges and Futures Commission Merchants (brokers) through which the Partnership trades.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P18_S0	The Partnership s financial statements are presented in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles ( U.S. GAAP ).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P18_S1	The preparation of the financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported fair value of assets and liabilities, disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities as of December 31, 2013 and 2012, and reported amounts of income and expenses for the years ended December 31, 2013, 2012 and 2011, respectively.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P18_S2	Management believes that the estimates utilized in preparing the Partnership s financial statements are reasonable; however, actual results could differ from these estimates and it is reasonably possible that the differences could be material.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P19_S0	In accordance with the authoritative guidance under U.S. GAAP, fair value is defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability (i.e. the exit price ) in an orderly transaction between market participants at the measurement date.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P20_S0	In determining fair value, the Partnership uses various valuation approaches.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P21_S0	The authoritative guidance under U.S. GAAP establishes a fair value hierarchy for inputs used in measuring fair value that maximizes the use of observable inputs and minimizes the use of unobservable inputs by requiring that the most observable inputs be used when available.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P22_S0	Observable inputs are those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability based on market data obtained from sources independent of the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P23_S0	Unobservable inputs reflect the Partnership s assumption about the inputs market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability developed based on the best information available in the circumstances.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P23_S1	The fair value hierarchy is categorized into three levels based on the inputs as follows:
1469317_14_ITEM15_P24_S0	Level 3 Prices, inputs or exotic modeling techniques which are both significant to the fair value measurement and unobservable (supported by little or no market activity).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P25_S0	The availability of valuation techniques and observable inputs can vary among assets and liabilities and is affected by a wide variety of factors, including the type of asset or liability, whether the asset or liability is new and not yet established in the marketplace, and other characteristics particular to the transaction.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P26_S0	To the extent that valuation is based on models or inputs that are less observable or unobservable in the market, the determination of fair value requires more judgment.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P26_S1	Those estimated values do not necessarily represent the amounts that may be ultimately realized due to the occurrence of future circumstances that cannot be reasonably determined.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P26_S2	Because of the inherent uncertainty of valuation, those estimated values may be materially higher or lower than the values that would have been used had a ready market for the asset or liability existed.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P26_S3	Accordingly, the degree of judgment exercised by the Partnership in determining fair value is greatest for assets and liabilities categorized in Level 3.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P27_S0	In certain cases, the inputs used to measure fair value may fall into different levels of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P27_S1	In such cases, for disclosure purposes, the level in the fair value hierarchy within which the fair value measurement falls in its entirety is determined by the lowest level input that is significant to the fair value measurement.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P28_S0	Fair value is a market-based measure considered from the perspective of a market participant rather than an entity-specific measure.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P28_S1	Therefore, even when market assumptions are not readily available, the Partnership s own assumptions are set to reflect those that market participants would use in pricing the asset or liability at the measurement date.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P29_S0	The Partnership uses prices and inputs that are current as of the measurement date, including prices and inputs during periods of market dislocation.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P29_S1	In periods of market dislocation, the observability of prices and inputs may be reduced for many assets and liabilities.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P29_S2	This condition could cause an asset or liability to be reclassified to a lower level within the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P30_S0	The Partnership values futures contracts at the closing price of the contract s primary exchange.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P30_S1	The Partnership includes futures contracts in Level 1 of the fair value hierarchy, as they are exchange traded derivatives.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P31_S0	The fair value of U.S. government agency bonds and notes is generally based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P31_S1	When quoted prices are not available, fair value is determined based on a valuation model that uses inputs which include interest-rate yield curves, cross-currency-basis index spreads, and country credit spreads similar to the bond in terms of issue, maturity and seniority.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P32_S0	U.S. government agency bonds and notes are categorized in Level I or Level 2 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P32_S1	As of December 31, 2013 and 2012 none of the Partnership s holdings in U.S. government agency bonds and notes were fair valued using valuation models.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P33_S0	The fair value of U.S. treasury obligations is generally based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P33_S1	U.S. treasury obligations are categorized in Level 1 of the fair value hierarchy.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P34_S0	The fair value of corporate notes is determined using recently executed transactions, market price quotations (where observable), notes spreads or credit default swap spreads.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P34_S1	The spread data used are for the same maturity as that of the notes.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P34_S2	If the spread data does not reference the issuer, data that references a comparable issuer is used.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P35_S0	When observable price quotations are not available, fair value is determined based on cash flow models with yield curves, notes, or single-name credit default swap spreads and recovery rates based on collateral values as key inputs.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P35_S1	These valuation methods represent both a market and income approach to fair value measurement.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P36_S0	Corporate notes are categorized in Level 2 of the fair value hierarchy; however, in instances where significant inputs are unobservable, they are categorized in Level 3 of the hierarchy.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P36_S1	As of December 31, 2013 and 2012 none of the Partnership s holdings in corporate notes were fair valued using valuation models.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P37_S0	The inputs or methodology used for valuing securities are not necessarily an indication of the risk associated with investing in those securities.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P37_S1	There were no changes in the Partnership s valuation methodology during the years ended December 31, 2013 and 2012.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P39_S0	"Financial Derivative Instruments" for the fair value in each type of contracts within this category.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P40_S0	For the years ended December 31, 2013 and 2012, there were no transfers between Level 1 and Level 2 assets and liabilities.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P40_S1	For the years ended December 31, 2013 and 2012, there were no Level 3 securities.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P41_S0	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date for financial reporting purposes.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P41_S1	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the specific identification cost method.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P41_S2	Change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the Statements of Income (Loss).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P42_S0	Brokerage commissions on securities and other trading fees are reflected as an adjustment to cost or proceeds at the time of the transaction.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P43_S0	Interest income is recorded on an accrual basis.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P44_S0	Gains or losses on futures contracts are realized when contracts are closed.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P44_S1	Net unrealized gains or losses on open contracts (the difference between contract trade price and quoted market price) are reflected in the Statements of Financial Condition.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P44_S2	Any change in net unrealized gain or loss from the preceding period is reported in the Statements of Income (Loss).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P45_S0	Brokerage commissions on futures contracts include other trading fees and are incurred as an expense when contracts are opened, and are recognized as trading gains and losses.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P46_S0	Net realized gains and losses from foreign currency related transactions represent gains and losses from sales of foreign currencies, sales and maturities of foreign currency forward contracts, currency gains and losses realized between trade and settlement dates on securities transactions, and the difference between the amounts of interest and foreign withholding taxes recorded on the Partnership s books and the U.S. Dollar equivalent of the amounts actually received or paid.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P46_S1	Net unrealized appreciation (depreciation) on foreign currency denominated other assets and liabilities arise from changes in the value of assets, other than investments in securities, and liabilities at fiscal year end, resulting from changes in the exchange rates.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P47_S0	JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A. (the Custodian ) is the Partnership s custodian.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P47_S1	The Partnership has cash deposited with the Custodian.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P47_S2	For cash not held with J.P. Morgan Securities, LLC, the Partnership s commodity broker (the Clearing Broker ), the Partnership receives cash management services from an affiliate of the Custodian, J.P. Morgan Investment Management Inc. ( JPMIM ).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P48_S0	The Partnership may engage in futures contracts as part of its investment strategy.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P49_S0	Upon entering into a futures contract, the Partnership is required to deposit with the broker an amount of cash or cash equivalents equal to a certain percentage of the contract amount.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P49_S1	This is known as the initial margin.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P49_S2	Subsequent payments ( variation margin ) are made or received by the Partnership each day, depending on the daily fluctuations in the value of the contract, and are included in unrealized gain (loss) on futures contracts.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P50_S0	The Partnership recognizes a realized gain or loss when the contract is closed.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P51_S0	There are several risks in connection with the use of futures contracts as an investment option.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P52_S0	The change in value of futures contracts primarily corresponds with the value of their underlying instruments.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P52_S1	In addition, there is the risk that the Partnership may not be able to enter into a closing transaction because of an illiquid secondary market.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P52_S2	Open positions in futures contracts at December 31, 2013 and 2012 are reflected within the Condensed Schedules of Investments.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P53_S0	The Partnership s functional currency is the U.S. dollar; however, it transacts business in currencies other than the U.S. dollar.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P53_S1	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the Statements of Financial Condition.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P53_S2	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P53_S3	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in the Statements of Income (Loss).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P54_S0	Restricted cash is held as maintenance margin deposits for futures transactions.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P55_S0	The Partnership maintains a custody account with a major financial institution.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P55_S1	At times, the Partnership s cash balance could exceed the insured amount under the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation ( FDIC ).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P55_S2	The Partnership has not experienced any losses in such accounts and believes it is not subject to any significant counterparty risk related to its cash account.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P56_S0	Offering costs incurred in connection with the ongoing offering of the Partnership s interests are borne by the Partnership.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P56_S1	These costs include, but are not limited to, legal fees pertaining to updating the Partnership s offering documents and materials, accounting and printing costs.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P56_S2	These costs are charged as an expense when incurred.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P58_S0	appeals or litigation processes, based on the technical merits of the position.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P59_S0	The tax benefit recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that has a greater than fifty percent likelihood of being realized upon ultimate settlement with the relevant taxing authority.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P59_S1	De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized results in the Partnership recording a tax liability that reduces ending partners capital.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P63_S2	Special Interests, Class A Interests, Class B Interests and Institutional Interests are then charged with their applicable management fee, administrative fee, service fee and incentive fee in accordance with the Agreement.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P64_S0	No limited partner of the Partnership (each, a Limited Partner and collectively the Limited Partners ) shall be liable for any debts or liabilities of the Partnership or any losses thereof in excess of such Limited Partner's capital contributions, except as may be required by law.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P65_S0	Investments in the Partnership are made by subscription agreement, subject to acceptance by the General Partner.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P66_S0	The Partnership is not required to make distributions, but may do so at the sole discretion of the General Partner.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P68_S0	The General Partner receives a monthly management fee from the Partnership equal to 0.104% (1.25% annually) for Class A and Class B, 0.0625% (0.75% annually) for Institutional Interests, and 0.0208% (0.25% annually) for Special Interests of the Partnership's management fee net asset value.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P68_S1	The General Partner may declare any Limited Partner a Special Limited Partner and the management fees or incentive fees charged to any such partner may be different than those charged to other Limited Partners.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P80_S0	If actual brokerage commissions paid to the Clearing Broker are less than the Minimum Amount, the Partnership will pay to the introducing broker, the difference.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P80_S1	However, if actual brokerage commissions are greater than the Minimum Amount, the Partnership only pays the actual brokerage commissions.

1469317_14_ITEM15_P92_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P92_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P92_S2	Further, the Clearing Broker has the right to require margin in excess of the minimum exchange requirement.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P92_S3	Risk arises from changes in the value of these contracts (market risk) and the potential inability of brokers to perform under the terms of their contracts (credit risk).
1469317_14_ITEM15_P93_S0	All of the contracts currently traded by the Partnership are exchange traded.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P93_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its respective individual counterparties.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P93_S2	However, in the future, if the Partnership were to enter into non-exchange traded contracts, it would be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P93_S3	The credit risk from counterparty non-performance associated with such instruments is the net unrealized gain, if any.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P94_S0	The Partnership also has credit risk because the sole counterparty to all domestic futures contracts is the exchange clearing corporation.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P94_S1	In addition, the Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by the Clearing Broker.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P95_S0	The Partnership's policy is to continuously monitor its exposure to market and counterparty risk through the use of a variety of financial, position and credit exposure reporting and control procedures.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P95_S1	In addition, the Partnership has a policy of reviewing the credit standing of each clearing broker or counterparty with which it conducts business.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P96_S0	The Partnership has a substantial portion of its assets on deposit with the Custodian in U.S. government agency bonds and notes and corporate notes.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P97_S0	Risks arise from investments in bonds and notes due to possible illiquidity and the potential for default by the issuer or counterparty.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P97_S1	Such instruments are also sensitive to changes in interest rates and economic conditions.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P98_S0	In the normal course of business, the Partnership enters into contracts and agreements that contain a variety of representations and warranties and which provide general indemnifications.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P98_S1	The Partnership s maximum exposure under these arrangements is unknown, as this would involve future claims that may be made against the Partnership that have not yet occurred.
1469317_14_ITEM15_P98_S2	The Partnership expects the risk of any future obligation under these indemnifications to be remote.

1469317_15_ITEM1_P0_S1	The Partnership is a commodity pool engaged in speculative trading across a broad range of futures contracts and currencies.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P0_S2	The Partnership may in the future trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts (together with futures contracts and currencies, Commodity Interests ).

1469317_15_ITEM1_P9_S2	Financial information regarding the Partnership s business is set forth in the Partnership s financial statements, included herewith.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P10_S0	The Partnership s objective is to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P11_S0	QIM believes that financial markets are not entirely efficient and that numerous small inefficiencies exist and can be exploited through the prudent use of robust analysis and predictive technologies.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P12_S0	QIM currently employs several thousand quantitative trading models that utilize pattern recognition to predict short-term price movements in global futures markets.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P12_S1	All models are tested across large data sets that expose them to a wide range of market, economic, and political environments, as well as a wide range of time frames and interactions.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P12_S2	Only those models that prove to be the most robust, statistically significant, and conceptually diverse are used in actual trading.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P12_S3	The resultant system of models offers what QIM believes to be reliable signals that guide market timing and trade allocation.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P13_S0	QIM s trading strategies and models may be revised from time to time as a result of ongoing research and development seeking to devise new strategies and systems as well as to improve current methods.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P13_S1	The strategies and systems used by QIM in the future may differ significantly from those currently in use due to changes resulting from this research, and Limited Partners will not be informed of these changes as they may occur.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P14_S0	QIM applies risk management procedures that take into account the price, size, volatility, liquidity, and inter-relationships of the contracts traded.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P14_S1	The Partnership s positions are generally balanced in a manner that allocates approximately equal amounts of measured risk to as many distinct markets as possible and during significant drawdowns in equity, QIM will reduce market exposure by scaling back the Partnership s overall leverage.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P15_S0	QIM s trading is generally approximately 95% systematic and 5% discretionary.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P15_S1	All facets of the predictive models, risk management, and trade allocation are fully automated or proceduralized.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P15_S2	In this sense, the trading is systematic.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P15_S3	Discretion of QIM, however, plays a significant role in the pursuit of improvements to the Program.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P16_S0	QIM has different time horizons for the execution of certain trades.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P16_S1	For example, QIM may have certain trades executed at the beginning of the trading day while giving the executing broker limited discretion with respect to other trades.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P17_S0	QIM currently trades or monitors a broad range of tradable markets in currencies, stock indices, interest rates, energy, grains, softs and metals.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P17_S1	QIM may add or delete markets from this universe of tradable markets in its discretion if QIM s research demonstrates that such an addition or deletion would enhance the program s performance.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P18_S0	All markets are futures markets or interbank currency markets.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P19_S0	QIM seeks to profitably trade each of these markets while taking advantage of the diversification available from such a varied universe of futures contracts.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P19_S1	QIM s trading program often takes opposing long and short positions within the same or related classes of correlated futures, which, taken in conjunction with the effect of diversification across a broad range of contracts, generally results in reduced market exposure than trading a single market with similar leverage.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P20_S0	A substantial portion of the equity in the Partnership s account is invested in United States ( U.S. ) government and agency securities and other liquid, high-quality instruments at the direction of the Custodian (as defined below).
1469317_15_ITEM1_P20_S1	QIM will generally maintain an average margin to equity level of between 0% and 20%.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P20_S2	The actual percentage of assets committed to margin at any time may be higher or lower than the target level.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P21_S0	It is expected that between 5% and 20% of the Partnership s assets generally will be held as initial margin or option premiums (in cash or U.S. Treasury Department ( Treasury ) securities) in the Partnership s brokerage accounts at its clearing broker, SG Americas Securities, LLC ( SGAS ), a futures commission merchant ( FCM ), and available for trading by QIM in Commodity Interests on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P21_S1	On January 2, 2015, Newedge USA, LLC ("Newedge USA") merged with and into SGAS, with the latter the surviving entity.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P22_S0	Interest on Partnership assets held at SGAS in cash or Treasury securities will be credited to the Partnership.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P22_S1	Depending on market factors, the amount of margin or option premiums held at SGAS could change significantly, and all of the Partnership s assets are available for use as margin.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P22_S2	The Partnership may also retain other brokers and/or dealers from time to time to clear or execute a portion of Partnership trades made by QIM.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P22_S3	In December 2014, the Partnership made SGAS its primary clearing broker.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P22_S4	J.P. Morgan Securities, LLC ("JPMS") has been retained to serve as a reserve clearing broker for the Partnership.

(the Custodian ), the portion not held in checking, money market or other bank accounts (and used to pay Partnership operating expenses) will be invested in liquid, high-quality short-term securities at the direction of the Custodian or its affiliate J.P. Morgan Investment Management Inc. ( JPMIM ).

1469317_15_ITEM1_P25_S0	The Partnership pays all of its ongoing liabilities, expenses and costs.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P25_S1	The General Partner receives a management fee of 0.104% of the month-end net asset value, before deduction for any accrued incentive fees related to the current quarter (the management fee net asset value ), of all Class A Interests (1.25% per annum), 0.104% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Class B Interests (1.25% per annum) and 0.0625% of the month-end management fee net asset value of all Institutional Interests (0.75% per annum).
1469317_15_ITEM1_P26_S0	QIM receives a 30% of quarterly trading profits applicable to each Class of Interest.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P27_S0	Each selling agent selling Class A Interests receives 0.166% of the month-end net asset value of the Partnership apportioned to each Class A Interest sold by such selling agent (2% per annum) and may elect to receive 0.0417% of the month-end net asset value apportioned to any Institutional Interest sold by such selling (0.50% per annum).

Morgan Securities paid during 2014 to Altegris Futures (which in December 2014 merged with and into the Introducing Broker) a portion of the brokerage commissions and transaction fees received from the Partnership as well as a portion of the interest income received on the Partnership s assets.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P29_S0	Monthly brokerage charges equal to the greater of (A) actual commissions of $9.75 per round-turn (higher for certain exchanges or commodities) multiplied by number of round-turn trades, which amount includes other transaction costs; or (B) an amount equal to 0.125% of the management fee net asset value of all Interest holders month-end capital account balances (1.50% annually).
1469317_15_ITEM1_P29_S1	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P29_S2	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership pays only the amount described in (A) above.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P30_S0	The Partnership generally pays its operating expenses as they are incurred.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P31_S0	A fixed administrative fee is charged to Class A and Class B Interests and paid to the General Partner equal to 0.0275% of the management fee net asset value of the month-end capital account balance of all such Class A and Class B Interests (0.333% per annum).
1469317_15_ITEM1_P32_S0	The CFTC has delegated to NFA responsibility for the registration of commodity trading advisors, commodity pool operators, futures commission merchants, introducing brokers, swap dealers , major swap participants and, in most cases, their respective associated persons, as well as floor brokers and floor traders.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P33_S0	The Commodity Exchange Act requires commodity pool operators such as the General Partner, commodity trading advisors such as the Advisor and commodity brokers or FCMs such as SGAS and introducing brokers such as the Introducing Broker to be registered and to comply with various reporting and record keeping requirements.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P33_S1	CFTC regulations also require FCMs and certain introducing brokers to maintain a minimum level of net capital.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P33_S2	In addition, the CFTC and certain commodities exchanges have established limits referred to as speculative position limits on the maximum net long or net short speculative positions that any person may hold or control in any particular futures or options contracts traded on U.S. commodities exchanges.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P33_S3	Similar position limits may in the future be put in place with respect to swaps that are exchange-traded or are economically equivalent to exchange-traded swaps or futures contracts.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P34_S0	All accounts owned or managed by the Advisor will be combined for position limit purposes.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P34_S1	The Advisor could be required to liquidate positions held for the Partnership in order to comply with such limits.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P34_S2	Any such liquidation could result in substantial costs to the Partnership.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P34_S3	In addition, many futures exchanges impose limits beyond which the price of a futures contract may not trade during the course of a trading day, and there is a potential for a futures contract to hit its daily price limit for several days in a row, making it impossible for the Advisor to liquidate a position and thereby experiencing a dramatic loss.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P35_S0	Certain deliverable currency forward contracts are subject to limited regulation in the United States, including reporting and recordkeeping requirements.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P36_S0	In addition to the registration requirements described above, the CFTC and certain commodity exchanges have established limits on the maximum net long or net short position which any person may hold or control in particular commodities.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P36_S1	Most exchanges also limit the changes in futures contract prices that may occur during a single trading day.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P36_S2	The CFTC may in the future also implement position limits for certain exempt commodity contracts, including metals and energy contracts, with respect to futures, options on futures, and economically equivalent swaps.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P36_S3	If such position limits are adopted, they could materially affect the Partnership s trading strategy.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P37_S0	Deliverable currency forward contracts are currently subject to only limited regulation in the United States.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P37_S1	The Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act (the Reform Act ) was enacted in July 2010, and gave the CFTC jurisdiction over non-deliverable currency forward contracts.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P37_S2	The Reform Act mandates that a substantial portion of over-the-counter derivatives must be executed in regulated markets and submitted for clearing to regulated clearinghouses, and the CFTC may impose such a requirement on non-deliverable currency forward contracts.
1469317_15_ITEM1_P37_S3	The mandates imposed by the Reform Act may result in the Partnership bearing higher upfront and mark-to-market margin, less favorable trade pricing, and the possible imposition of new or increased fees with respect to any swaps entered into by the Partnership.

1469317_15_ITEM1_P38_S1	The Partnership does not engage in sales of goods or services.

1469317_15_ITEM7_P1_S0	The Partnership s assets are generally held as cash or cash equivalents, which are used to margin the Partnership s futures positions and are sold to pay redemptions and expenses as needed.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P1_S1	Other than any potential market-imposed limitations on liquidity, the Partnership s assets are highly liquid and are expected to remain so.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P1_S2	Market-imposed limitations, when they occur, can be due to limited open interest in certain futures markets or to daily price fluctuation limits, which are inherent in the Partnership s futures trading.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P2_S0	A portion of the Partnership s assets not used for margin and held with the Custodian are invested in liquid, high quality securities.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P2_S1	Through December 31, 2014 the Partnership experienced no meaningful periods of illiquidity in any of the markets traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P3_S0	The Partnership raises additional capital only through the sale of Interests and capital is increased through trading profits (if any) and interest income.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P3_S1	The Partnership does not engage in borrowing.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P4_S0	The amount of capital raised for the Partnership should not have a significant impact on its operations, as the Partnership has no significant capital expenditure or working capital requirements other than for capital to pay trading losses, brokerage commissions and expenses.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P4_S1	Within broad ranges of capitalization, the Partnership s trading positions should increase or decrease in approximate proportion to the size of the Partnership.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P5_S0	The Partnership participates in the speculative trading of commodity futures contracts and may trade options on futures contracts and forward contracts, substantially all of which are subject to margin requirements.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P5_S1	The minimum amount of margin required for each contract is set from time to time in response to various market factors by the respective exchanges.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P5_S2	Further, the Partnership s FCMs and brokers may require margin in excess of minimum exchange requirements.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P6_S0	All of the futures contracts currently traded by the Advisor on behalf of the Partnership are exchange-traded.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P6_S1	The risks associated with exchange-traded contracts are generally perceived to be less than those associated with over-the-counter transactions because, in over-the-counter transactions, the Partnership must rely solely on the credit of its trading counterparties, whereas exchange-traded contracts are generally, but not universally, backed by the collective credit of the members of the exchange.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P6_S2	In the future, the Partnership anticipates that it will enter into non-exchange-traded foreign currency contracts and be subject to the credit risk associated with counterparty non-performance.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P7_S0	The Partnership bears the risk of financial failure by SGAS and/or other clearing brokers or counterparties with which the Partnership trades.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P8_S0	The Partnership s success depends primarily upon QIM s ability to recognize and capitalize on market trends in the sectors of the global commodity futures markets in which it trades.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P8_S1	The Partnership seeks to produce long-term capital appreciation through growth, and not current income.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P8_S2	The past performance of the Partnership is not necessarily indicative of future results.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P9_S0	During 2014, the Partnership achieved net realized and unrealized losses of $8,510,727 from all trading; losses of $8,523,461 from trading of commodity futures contracts including brokerage commissions of $949,065.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P9_S1	The Partnership incurred total expenses of $2,032,676, including $5,124 in incentive fees, $747,326 in management fees paid to the General Partner, and $956,163 in service and professional fees.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P9_S2	The Partnership earned $56,273 in interest income during 2014.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P9_S3	An analysis of the profits and losses generated from the Partnership s commodity futures trading activities for each quarter during 2014 is set forth below.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P10_S0	The Partnership experienced a loss in October 2014 with the bulk of the poor performance driven by short positions in futures contracts on the S P, Dax and DJ Euro Stoxx 50 stock indices.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P10_S1	Performance was further degraded by short positions in futures contracts on the Euro-Bund.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P11_S0	The Partnership experienced gains during the month from its short positions in futures contracts on Crude Oil.

1469317_15_ITEM7_P37_S0	The General Partner believes that the Partnership s most critical accounting estimates relate to the valuation of the Partnership s assets.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P38_S0	Futures and options on futures contracts are valued using the primary exchange s closing price.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P38_S1	U.S. government agency securities are generally valued based on quoted prices in active markets.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P38_S2	Corporate notes are generally valued at fair value.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P38_S3	Security transactions are recorded on the trade date.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P38_S4	Realized gains and losses from security transactions are determined using the specific identification cost method.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P39_S0	Assets and liabilities denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect at the date of the statement of financial condition.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P39_S1	Income and expense items denominated in currencies other than the U.S. dollar are translated into U.S. dollars at the rates in effect during the period.
1469317_15_ITEM7_P39_S2	Gains and losses resulting from the translation to U.S. dollars are reported in income currently.

1469317_15_ITEM9A_P0_S0	(a) The General Partner, with the participation of the General Partner s principal executive officer and principal financial officer, has evaluated the effectiveness of the design and operation of its disclosure controls and procedures with respect to the Partnership as of the end of the period covered by this annual report, and, based on their evaluation, has concluded that these disclosure controls and procedures are effective.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P1_S0	Altegris Advisors, L.L.C., the general partner of the Partnership, is responsible for the management of the Partnership.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P1_S1	Management of the General Partner ( Management ) is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P1_S2	The internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use or disposition of the Partnership s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P3_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P3_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P4_S0	Management assessed the effectiveness of the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting as of December 31, 2014.
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P4_S1	In making this assessment, Management used the criteria set forth in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission ( COSO ).
1469317_15_ITEM9A_P4_S2	As a result of this assessment and based on the criteria in the COSO framework, management has concluded that, as of December 31, 2014, the Partnership s internal control over financial reporting was effective.

1469317_15_ITEM11_P3_S1	If actual monthly commissions and transaction costs in (A) above are less than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay the difference to the Introducing Broker as payment for brokerage-related services.
1469317_15_ITEM11_P3_S2	In any month when the amount in (A) is greater than the amount in (B) above, the Partnership will pay only the amount described in (A) above.

1469317_15_ITEM15_P16_S0	The Partnership speculatively trades commodity futures contracts, and may trade options on futures contracts, forward contracts and other commodity interests.
1469317_15_ITEM15_P17_S0	The objective of the Partnership s business is appreciation of its assets.
1469317_15_ITEM15_P17_S1	It is subject to the regulations of the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (the CFTC ), an agency of the United States ( U.S. ) government that regulates most aspects of the commodity futures industry; rules of the National Futures Association, an industry self-regulatory organization; and the requirements of commodity exchanges and futures commission merchants (brokers) through which the Partnership trades.
